Letter from the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Bureau 79

In your newspaper on the fifth of this month, on page eleven of the third section, there was a Central News Agency dispatch titled "Construction Status of the Nanyu Section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway." The content stated that the track laying had reached Zexi, but due to the poor soil quality between Yushan and Shangrao, derailments were frequent. Therefore, the opening of the line and ticket sales between Shangrao and Guixi would be temporarily suspended. However, the track-laying work of our railway currently only extends to the vicinity of Hengfeng, and trains are running smoothly to Shangrao. The information in your newspaper does not correspond with the facts, and we are deeply concerned about misunderstandings. We are writing this special letter to request that you publish a correction. Sincerely, Shanghai Shenbao Newspaper Office, Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Bureau, September 7th.

Hong Kong-Guangdong: Guangdong Bank Suspends Operations; Finance Department Seals Guangdong Branch; Long-Term and Recent Causes of Suspension 80

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangdong Bank was founded in the first year of the Republic of China. Its head office is located in Hong Kong and registered with the British Hong Kong government as Guangdong Bank Limited. It has a capital of 11 million yuan, with a paid-up capital of 8,665,600 yuan, with shares at 40 yuan each. Branches are located in Guangzhou, Shanghai, Hankou, Taishan, and San Francisco, Siam, and other places. Unexpectedly, on the 4th of this month, the Guangdong Bank branch at No. 6 Des Voeux Road Central, Hong Kong, suddenly announced its suspension of business and posted a notice at the entrance stating, "Due to the impact of the economic recession, this bank is temporarily suspending payments pending reorganization." On the same day (the 4th) at 10:00 am, the Guangzhou branch of Guangdong Bank on Xidi in Guangzhou was also heavily locked, with branch staff fleeing and a notice posted stating, "Following a telegram from the head office, due to the global economic recession in recent years, it is impossible to maintain operations. The board of directors has resolved to temporarily suspend business from the 4th and await reorganization. Guangdong Bank Guangzhou Branch." Before the Guangzhou branch suspended operations, there had been a run on the bank. On the 3rd, depositors withdrew hundreds of thousands of yuan in cash. After the branch suspended operations, the provincial government, upon receiving a report, dispatched accountants Zhao Zhuo, Chief of Section Liu Baochi, and Cheng Mengyang from the Finance Department, along with the responsible police sub-bureau, to count the number of ledger books in the branch. However, when they arrived, the staff had already left, and none of the account books were present. The silver vault, iron boxes, and safes were open, making it impossible to inspect them. They immediately reported back to the Finance Department Director Qu Fangpu, who, on the grounds that the bank's suspension had not been reported in advance and that no responsible person was in charge, immediately sealed the branch together with the Public Security Bureau for liquidation and issued an arrest warrant for important branch personnel to be brought to justice.

It is understood that the general manager of the bank's head office is Lu Pengshan, the deputy general manager is Li Zizhong, and the manager of the Guangzhou branch is Chen Shanming. They have all left the mainland. According to those familiar with the bank's situation, for more than twenty years, the bank's operations in Guangdong have made it a giant among commercial banks, with branches spread across various ports. Since the global economic downturn, remittances from overseas Chinese have plummeted, leading to a decline in business. Furthermore, since the United States implemented its silver policy, exchange rates have been volatile. At the same time, silver deposits have become rare, while withdrawals have been continuous. In total, over the past three years, depositors have withdrawn no less than 17 to 18 million yuan. This has made the bank appear strong on the outside but weak on the inside. Moreover, the bank's investments in the past have not been recovered recently, and most of the real estate mortgages have not been redeemed. Furthermore, real estate prices have fallen recently, making it even more difficult to liquidate assets. The bank has repeatedly suffered from these problems, and withdrawals have continued unabated, leading to its inability to maintain operations. A few days ago, the board of directors resolved to suspend operations pending reorganization. The bank currently has real estate worth approximately 8 million yuan, and [unclear] will increase its capital by a certain amount in an attempt to resume operations. However, the exact amount of its foreign debt is unknown, and whether it can be cleared is still uncertain. (Evening of September 4th)

Zhang Qun Returns to Hankou from Nanjing; Meets with Liu Zhenhua En Route to Discuss Border Demarcation Issues; This Year's Floods Have Already Attracted Attention from Both Government and Public 81

Hankou Correspondence: Provincial Governor Zhang Qun went to Lushan in the middle of last month to visit Chairman Lin and Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to report on the disaster situation in Hubei Province and request relief. Later, he was entrusted by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to go to Qingdao to represent him in expressing condolences to the sick President Zhu and to urge him to return to Nanjing to resume his duties. After President Zhu returned from his leave, Zhang Qun rushed to Nanjing and Shanghai to negotiate disaster relief. On the 5th of this month, Zhang Qun finished his official business in Nanjing and took a plane back west. He stopped in Anqing, disembarked to visit Liu Zhenhua, and discussed the issue of border demarcation between the three provinces of Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui. That evening, he boarded the Longhe ship westward. When passing Jiujiang, Xiong Shihui boarded the ship to meet with him and discuss the border demarcation issue. Zhang arrived in Hankou by the same ship at 4:00 pm on the 7th. According to Zhang's statement, "During my trip to Nanjing, I appealed on behalf of the disaster victims. The central authorities expressed great sympathy and felt that the water management problem was related to the people's livelihood and national economy and must be addressed both fundamentally and symptomatically. On the 3rd of this month, the Executive Yuan passed measures to address river flooding both fundamentally and symptomatically. The fundamental aspect involves dredging, management, and returning reclaimed land to lakes to reduce river flow, using surcharges on customs duties, transportation surcharges, and land taxes as funding. The symptomatic aspect involves resuming work and closing breaches, with the National Economic Council responsible for the projects and funding to be raised by the central government and civil servant salary donations. It can be said that the measures have been determined and are awaiting implementation. Rumors that the central government will issue 90 million yuan in disaster relief bonds are unfounded. The disaster relief work in this province has also been decided to address both fundamentally and symptomatically, with emergency relief for farmers and addressing the symptoms, and work relief for fundamental solutions. The funds for emergency relief for farmers will be raised by this province and donations from various parties, while the National Economic Council will allocate 3 million yuan for work relief. This time, Hubei Province accounted for the majority of the Yangtze River levee breaches. Just taking the breach of the Zhongxian San Si Gong levee as an example, the cost of repairing it will require millions. The planned 3 million yuan may not be enough. In the past, the people of this province believed that major floods only occurred once every few decades. Unexpectedly, only four years after the major flood of the 1920s, there was an even greater flood this year. The superstitious mentality of the past has been shattered, and people are now keenly aware of the possibility of floods in the coming years and are eager to prevent them. The central authorities are also paying special attention to addressing both fundamentally and symptomatically, so this year's flood can be said to be a blessing in disguise, as it has promoted unified attention from both the government and the public. Furthermore, there are many embankments in this province. In the past, there was a distinction between official embankments and civilian embankments. For example, the Zhang Gong Embankment, which protects Hankou, is an official embankment, while the Wuhui Embankment, which protects Wuchang, is a civilian embankment. In the future, the central government is determined to address the fundamental issues, unify the national water conservancy agencies, and coordinate the work, which will naturally eliminate the dispute between officials and civilians and achieve a unified flood prevention effect. After hearing this news, the people will also be slightly reassured. The issue of border demarcation between the three provinces is also related to water conservancy. The Mahua Embankment spans the borders of Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui provinces. In the past, the annual repair costs were shared by the three provinces, with Hubei Province responsible for 56%, Anhui Province responsible for 31%, and [unclear] Province responsible for 11%. Due to regional jurisdiction issues, investigations and arguments were quite inconvenient, so negotiations on border demarcation were held to resolve this [unclear] difficulty. As for the province's depleted finances, we originally wanted to seek assistance from the central government, but the central government has exhausted its efforts in this disaster relief effort. It is also inconvenient to report local financial difficulties to the central government again. We can only try to save money and seek [unclear] expenditure. (September 7th)

Chen Zhaoying Inspects Southwestern Fujian 82

—Also sends letter to Provincial Government to postpone collection of land tax in disaster areas—

Fuzhou Correspondence: Provincial Party [unclear] Special Commissioner and Fujian-Zhejiang Inspector Chen Zhaoying, on August 18th, led more than ten staff members to inspect various counties in southwestern Fujian, passing through Fuqing, Putian, Huian, Jinjiang, Nan'an, Tong'an, Longxi, and Longyan counties. He returned to the province on the 6th of this month. According to him, this trip involved traveling by water to Xiamen, then to Zhangzhou, and returning to the province by land, taking about two weeks. Because the transportation in various counties in southern Fujian is convenient, an average of one county was inspected per day. Moreover, the local people were very attentive to my inspection mission, so the work was very convenient wherever I went. When discovering illegal acts by civil servants, I immediately requested the relevant responsible officials to correct and punish them. Currently, the public security in various counties, townships, and districts is becoming more peaceful. In terms of official governance, as long as the county magistrate is competent, the heads of various townships, districts, and [unclear] guarantee directors will be able to follow orders and will not deceive their superiors or hide things from them. It has been found that the general public in various counties in southern Fujian are most pained by the collection of militia fees, because they are arbitrary and severely disrupt the people's lives. It is heard that the heads of various districts and townships and the directors of the joint guarantee system manipulate the fees, and the burden on the people often exceeds the prescribed amount by several times. The government receives very little, but the harm to the people is great. The Provincial Government and the Pacification Office will soon find a way to coordinate this militia fee in southern Fujian. I previously met with Finance Director Xu in Zhangzhou and discussed this matter. At the latest, it can be implemented by the end of October. During this inspection, a total of more than 180 documents were received, mostly concerning requests to abolish exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies, extra collections, and those who extort bribes. There were also prisoners complaining about injustice and requesting improved prison treatment. It is said that I will continue to inspect northern and eastern Fujian in the future. In addition, Chen stated that this year, after two hurricanes and floods, the extent of the disaster area and the severity of the disaster are unprecedented in recent decades. In particular, Jinjiang, Nan'an, Anxi, Longxi, Shao'an, Huian, Changtai, and Lianjiang counties have suffered the most severe disasters. All the late-season land taxes in the affected counties and fees for reporting and verifying contracts should be allowed to be postponed to alleviate the people's distress and show compassion. He has sent a letter to the provincial government requesting verification and handling. After the provincial government approved the letter, it asked the first, fourth, fifth, and sixth administrative commissioners to quickly investigate and report the extent of the disaster in Lianjiang and other counties after the two hurricanes and floods, and whether there was any loss of land and property, in order to verify and handle the matter. (September 7th)

The Water Level in Tongbei is Increasing; The Situation in Fengpei is Also Tense; The Southern Embankment of the Bulao River Breached 83

Xuzhou Correspondence: After the water from Weishan Lake in Tongbei breached the Weishan Lake West Embankment at the Lanjiaba breach and reached Wanzhai, the water that flooded west was contained by the surrounding embankment, and the water that flowed east discharged along the Jing River. The Chedaokou Embankment was located directly to the south and was initially stable. Unexpectedly, the water rose sharply again one day, first breaching the opening of the canal at Wanzhai. The water flooded the canal and irrigated Chedaokou. Chedaokou is the mouth of the canal entering Machang Lake, and the water broke through the dam opening and poured into Machang Lake. This place is eight miles away from Chengbu, and the people were very alarmed for a time. The county government ordered Wu Jianqiu, the chief of the first district, to supervise 5,000 villagers from the Huangshan, Huangmao, Duanzhuang, and Bali villages to rush to plug the breach day and night. The dam opening had been newly added with stone masonry, but the stones were washed away by the water, the dam foundation subsided, and sacks were hastily used to block it. The breach was reported to have been blocked after two days, but water still seeped through the cracks between the stones. The people of Wanzhai were surrounded by water because of the breach at the canal opening. Now, ships from Weishan Lake are directly docked outside Li Village, and there is great fear that if the water increases again, the whole village will become fish. Therefore, the strengthening of the Wanzhai canal mouth dam is continuing, with lights shining all night and work continuing non-stop. The water flow has now been reduced, and Wanzhai Village can be protected. At the same time, the river mouth at Wutun on the west surrounding embankment was breached very widely, and the water flooded west from the opening. County Magistrate Wang Gong and others rushed to supervise the defense and gathered villagers to build an eight-mile-long outer surrounding embankment to the west of the river mouth to contain the water. The water flowing east also breached the east section of the Jinpu Transverse Embankment at the south end of Jingshan Bridge. The water flowed to Wangzhuang, and Wu Jianqiu, the chief of the first district, also dispatched 1,000 villagers to rush to plug the breach, which has been plugged. Although the embankments in Tongbei are constantly in danger, they can still contain the water by adding construction at any time. However, it is especially feared that the water will continue to rise and cause problems.

After the disaster in Tongbei, the situation in Fengpei was slightly stable. Now, the water level upstream of Weishan Lake continues to rise. In addition, from the evening of the 2nd to the evening of the 4th, the wind was blowing from east to west, and the entire west embankment of Weishan Lake was reported to be tight. The Peidong Jizhuang was breached by water, and Huzhai, Xiewu, and other places were also under pressure. Yang Guozhen, the newly appointed magistrate of Pei County, and Yu Keyu, the section chief sent by the special office to Fengpei, and members of the Yellow River Prevention Association all set out and finished plugging the breaches without any danger. Wang Shuxian, the magistrate of Feng County, came to Xuzhou the day before yesterday and said that the water situation in Feng County was slightly more stable than in Pei County. Recently, the water breach in Yutai has been increasing unabated, and the north embankment is also showing signs of danger. Fengpei is purchasing sackcloth for use in Xuzhou. The sackcloth and cattail bags in the Xuzhou market have been completely sold out.

The Bulao River is the lower reaches of the Jing River. The upper reaches are called the Yan River during the day, but it is actually one river that changes its name three times. The water from Weishan Lake discharges through the Yan River and Jing River in Tongbei. The riverbed is shallow, but the water volume is huge, and most of the banks are overflowing. Therefore, the Bulao River bank embankment was built. Unexpectedly, the water was even more fierce in the lower reaches. On the 3rd, a breach occurred near Kouzhuang and Wadianzi in the sixth district of Tongdong. The water flowed south, and the breach was more than forty feet wide with a large volume of water. After flowing south, it turned east. Therefore, in addition to the disaster in the sixth district where the breach occurred, more than ten villages in the ninth district were also flooded. The ninth district office is located in Xiaotashan. As the water flooded into the district, Wang Shuren, the head of the district, rushed to move the district office to a nearby earthen enclosure to avoid the flood and facilitate command. There is the Fangting River in the ninth district, which is the source of water for Tongdong's water conservancy. The breached water flowed into the river channel, the river water overflowed, and the land between the rivers was all flooded. The water then flowed east from here, leaving Tongdong and entering Pi County. Yesterday, according to Pi County News, it has reached Bayi Ji. Bayi Ji is located south of the Longhai Railway and is an important market town in the eastern section. Pinan has also been affected by the disaster. (5th)

Songjiang: Prostitution and Abduction Case Discovered in Hotel

Huang Xigui, a patrol officer from the Sijing Public Security Sub-Station, was checking hotels last night when he found three men and women with different accents in room 10 of the Central Hotel. They seemed suspicious, and after detailed questioning, he discovered that the case involved prostitution and abduction. One man, Wu Bingsheng, from Changzhou, had seduced Li A [unclear], a woman from Huizhou who worked as a servant in Panjiaqiao, Xujiahui. They had spent one night together in Xujiahui. He came to Si today intending to arrange a marriage. Another man, Wang Guizhong, from Shanghai, denied conspiring to abduct the woman, saying that he had been invited by Wu Bingsheng to Si for fun. The woman confessed that she worked as a servant in Shanghai and had returned to her hometown once. She had recently come to Shanghai and worked as a servant in Xujiahui when she was seduced by Wu, etc. The case was related to criminal matters and was taken to the station for interrogation today.

Jinshan: Resignation of Captain Fan

Jinshan is located near the coast, and bandits frequently appear. Since Fan Zhicheng, the captain of the first team of the first district of the Jiangsu Maritime Public Security Team, was stationed in Zhu, he has repeatedly destroyed bandit dens and captured major bandits, such as Taibao A [unclear], Zhuluo A Mei, and Gaojiao Pai A Si, all of whom were captured by Captain Fan through information and capture. The local people celebrated this. His most outstanding achievements in suppressing bandits include rescuing 31 hostages from Zhang [unclear] and 9 hostages from Ganpu. All the bandits were also captured. His achievements were also great. It is now heard that he has resolutely resigned due to organizational reasons and handed over his duties the day before yesterday. People from all walks of life regret this for the local area.

Suzhou: Farmers in Xiangtian Township Report Crop Failure

Since the summer and autumn of this year, the rice crops in the four rural areas have been thriving due to suitable rainfall. Unexpectedly, since the beginning of autumn, there have been frequent gales and showers. The rice seedlings in various townships were just bearing fruit, so they were greatly affected. The rice paddies in Xiangcheng and Jiajing and other villages outside Loumen suffered severe damage. The seedlings were destroyed by wind and rain, resulting in failure to bear fruit, and the quality is bound to be greatly reduced. Yesterday morning, more than fifty farmers from various villages came to the city with withered yellow rice straw to report crop failure to the relevant owners and the county government, requesting them to send personnel to investigate and reduce rent, taxes, and land prices.

The Young Owner of a Private Bank Commits Suicide in Suzhou

Peng Zhaosong, the 26-year-old young owner of Tongtai Private Bank in Nanda Street, Ruian, Wenzhou, was married. He went to Hangzhou to seek employment due to abuse by his stepmother. However, his fate was not good, and he did not find a job in three months. He planned to go north to visit Commander Yu of the 58th Division of the Army to find a position. However, he was penniless, so he sent a letter from Hangzhou to his father, Weizhong, asking for travel expenses. He then received a reply from his father, severely reprimanding him and ordering him to return home immediately. As a result, Peng Zhaosong was deeply stimulated. On the 5th, he came to Suzhou from Hangzhou and stayed at room 22 of the Jiaotong Hotel outside Guanmen. He secretly purchased poison. Because it was inconvenient to take poison in the hotel, he went out in the evening and hailed a rickshaw to Daoqian Street. He took the poison in the rickshaw. He was poisoned and unconscious when he was dragged to Daoqian Street. He was discovered by a police officer on duty and sent to the hospital for treatment. He was revived. He was then sent from the hospital to the Second Public Security Bureau. Yesterday, the Second Public Security Bureau telegraphed his family to come to Suzhou to take him back. At that time, the mountain police station found two suicide notes beside him, which were temporarily stored in the bureau.

Four Families Robbed Consecutively in the Countryside of Wujiang

On the night of the 7th, eight or nine robbers suddenly arrived at the home of Hu Jinfu, a villager in Liuxu Village, Gu Liu Township, Wujiang County. They were armed and robbed. They tied up Hu's wife, Shen, and forced her to reveal the location of the hidden money. Shen was tied up, beaten, and urine was poured into her mouth with a pot. The situation was extremely miserable. The robbers then went to rob the homes of Xu Laotai, Ding Jinbao, and Ding Baolin. At that time, the villagers of Tongli Township wanted to come out and resist, but they did not dare to speak out because the robbers fired shots as a demonstration. It is estimated that the robbery lasted for about two hours, and the robbers left with their loot. The four families lost about five to six hundred yuan.

Wuxi: The Zhenxin Labor Strike Has Reached a Deadlock

The labor-management dispute at the Zhenxin Yarn Factory in Taibaodun, outside the West Gate, has reached a deadlock despite the intervention of party and government agencies for mediation because no one is responsible on the factory side, making mediation difficult. It is now learned that 411 employees of the Ministry of Industry, including Gong Zhiping and Yu Weiqing, are cut off from their livelihoods. In addition to sending a letter to Manager Jiang Zeqing requesting the payment of their August salaries, they also sent a separate letter to the Zhenxin Board of Directors requesting relief, asking them to issue severance pay to barely survive if the resumption of work is indefinite.

Ding Chaowu Comes to Wuxi for Secret Investigation

After taking office, Ding Chaowu, the Jiangsu Regional Inspector of the National Government's Control Yuan, planned to inspect various counties in southern Jiangsu. However, due to the Yellow River floods in various counties in northern Jiangsu, he first went to various counties in northern Jiangsu to investigate the disaster situation. After completing his official duties, he returned to the province for a brief rest. A few days ago, he set off with his staff member Guo Hongzhong to inspect Wujiang and Wuxian counties, secretly investigating various cases. He then went to Changshu to inspect the county government, county prison, and business tax bureau, and inquired about various accusations in detail. He hired a car on the Wuxi-Shanghai highway from Yu the night before last and came to Wuxi for inspection incognito. His whereabouts were extremely secret, so very few outsiders knew about it. After Ding secretly completed his investigation in Wuxi, he will transfer to Yichang and other counties for inspection.

Yangzhou: The Court Searches the Sian Public Office

In the case of salt merchant Zhu Shiwu and others suing the staff of the Sian Public Office for embezzlement and breach of trust in the Jiangdu Court, only the allegation of embezzlement was involved, totaling more than 370,000 yuan. The court had sent personnel to search and found a large amount of evidence and held several court hearings. New evidence has now been discovered. On the 7th, Wang Jiaxiang, a clerk from the court, along with Wang Baoquan, a police chief, and Zhang Yueqiao, a bailiff, and Yang Dixiang, a patrol officer from the First Public Security Sub-Station, and police officers and guards, went to the Sian Public Office for a search. Under the eyes of Feng San, a worker from the public office, they searched the premises and found five books of ledgers for Huainan merchants borrowing money and allocating it to offset salt taxes, and settling interest, and sixteen various documents, drafts, approvals, and edicts for borrowing and paying tax money and requesting interest payment. They took them to the court to report.

Dockworkers Demand Expedited Handling: Transportation

The fan transportation in Shier Xu has been suspended since April of this year, and the livelihoods of Jiangxi boat workers have been at a loss. The Joint Association of Salt Affairs Groups specially appointed representatives Duan Zhizhou and Chen Zhensheng to come to Yangzhou to request the Sian Public Office and the Xiang Merchants Association to expedite the handling of fan transportation to solve their immediate needs. However, many important figures among the salt merchants were not in [unclear] and could not reply immediately. It is reported that Duan and others visited a certain Liu of the Xiang Merchants, who said that the merchants were also in a difficult situation, and that Xu and Yangzhou were both in the same predicament. The dockworkers' suffering was indeed real, and the merchants hoped that Xu could understand their difficulties. As for the request to expedite the handling of fan transportation, they agreed to discuss it after the merchants returned to Yangzhou. Duan and others asked them to convey their intentions to the merchants and requested a written reply on the results of this trip. A decision will be made after the public office meeting.

Hangzhou: Highway Bureau Orders Charcoal Cars

In order to promote domestic production and save consumption, the Highway Bureau of Zhejiang Province held a charcoal car competition. The result was that the Zhongming Company was the best. It ordered ten charcoal cars from the company, which will arrive in Hangzhou in the middle of the month. After complete assembly, they will run on the Beijing-Hangzhou, Shanghai-Hangzhou, and Hangzhou-Anhui roads. At the same time, they will resume the trial use of domestic car tires and engine oil to prevent leakage.

Local News

Catholic Action Association National Delegates Conference Opened Yesterday Morning; Archbishop Tsai Ning Read Papal Message; Mayor Wu Addressed, Hoping to Save Self and Save Others 85

The National Diocesan Delegates Conference of the Chinese Catholic Action Association was held yesterday morning at 10 o'clock in the auditorium of Zhengxiu Middle School on Guohuo Road in the Nanshi district. Over two hundred people attended, including Archbishop Tsai Ning, diocesan bishops from across the country, and representatives. Guests included Mayor Wu and over a hundred Shanghai citizens who attended freely. The following is a record of the opening ceremony:

Over Two Hundred Representatives from Various Regions

The representatives of the various dioceses attending the conference got up at 5 o'clock yesterday morning. At 5:30, they went to the hall together to listen to the principles of retreat, attend Mass, and receive Holy Communion. At 8 o'clock, they returned to Puyutang to participate in Archbishop Tsai's solemn Mass, especially seeking the intercession of Saint Joseph. At 10 o'clock, they entered the Zhengxiu auditorium together to hold the opening ceremony. A total of Archbishop Tsai Ning, twenty-one diocesan bishops from across the country, and over two hundred diocesan priests and representatives from across the country were present. Guests included Mayor Wu, representative Tsai Jinjun, Wang Dasui, and over a hundred citizens who attended freely.

Archbishop Tsai Ning Delivered Opening Address

At the opening of the conference, Lu Bohong served as chairman and Archbishop Tsai Ning as supervisor. First, the Zhengxiu Middle School string band played the national anthem, followed by Archbishop Tsai Ning standing up to recite the invocation of the Holy Spirit and bowing three times to the national and religious flags. Then, the conference song was sung, and Pope's representative Archbishop Tsai Ning read the Pope's personal letter (omitted) and delivered an opening address. In brief: (1) Thanks to the Holy Spirit for bestowing blessings on humanity; (2) Thanks to Bishop Hui of the Shanghai region for his able leadership, achieving today's success; (3) Thanks to Mayor Wu of Greater Shanghai for personally attending and instructing; (4) Thanks to the representatives of various dioceses for their efforts in religious affairs;

Catholic Action Association National Delegates Conference Opening (International News Agency Photo) efforts to spread the Gospel; (5) Thanks to Chairman Lu and the entire organizing committee, and the enthusiastic participation of the representatives from various dioceses. He also mentioned that the Pope had received Chinese aviation graduates and personally instructed them, "You are the new youth of China. At the same time, you are learning to fly upward. I hope you will strive to fly upward and help all Chinese compatriots fly upward with you." Based on this instruction from the Pope, we ourselves must fly upward and help all Chinese compatriots fly upward. This is what is meant by perfecting oneself and perfecting others. If one can be a good Catholic, one is a good citizen. Representatives should strive to act in accordance with the Pope's intentions, especially members of the Catholic Action Association, who should strive to create blessings for themselves and for humanity based on this idea.

Mayor's Speech: Congratulating on Success

Mayor Wu delivered a speech saying, "Today, the National Diocesan Delegates Conference of the Chinese Catholic Action Association is being held. As the Mayor of Shanghai, I am here to attend the opening ceremony and express my slight congratulations. At the same time, I welcome Archbishop Tsai Ning, the representatives from various dioceses, and all members of the Catholic Action Association. Catholicism has been in China for hundreds of years, and it has undertaken many charitable, educational, and social endeavors. The Chinese people have benefited greatly from Catholicism. As for the Chinese Catholic Action Association, I have heard that it has only been established for three years, and today's conference is the first one. 'Catholic Action' means action. Therefore, we must not only have faith but also take action. We must not only have faith ourselves but also put our faith into practice. We must not only practice ourselves to seek understanding but also hope that everyone can gain understanding through practice. We may enjoy spiritual and material comfort, but others are not able to enjoy such comfort. We believe in Catholicism and find peace ourselves, but other people cannot find peace. Therefore, we must save ourselves and also save others. Therefore, we must not only do good ourselves but also help others do good. The Chinese people have received many kinds of teachings, but unfortunately, they are not in line with the times. Therefore, I believe that it is not enough to cultivate oneself alone; one must also help others. It is useless for one person to be good; it is only useful if everyone is good. Since Catholicism came to China, in addition to spreading the Gospel, it has also done a lot of charitable work for our Chinese Catholics to see. Now, Chinese Catholics have organized the Chinese Catholic Action Association and are holding a national diocesan delegates conference. Its significance is very great. The Chinese Catholic Action Association is to tell Catholics across the country that not only can individuals seek liberation, but the entire majority of people must be able to achieve liberation, and especially to be consistent in word and deed, because if words are false, then faith is also false. If words and deeds can be consistent, then faith can become true, and thus it can have an effect. Today, the Chinese Catholic Action Association is holding a national diocesan delegates conference to study and discuss how to implement various Catholic works in China in the future. I hope that the diocesan representatives, in addition to reporting on the situation of religious affairs, should also report on the social situation of each region to the conference, so that the conference can understand the real situation in order to make decisions and improve Chinese society, education, and various charitable undertakings. Finally, I hope the conference will be a success."

Hui Lu Delivered Address: Stating the Mission

Then, Bishop Hui of the Shanghai area delivered a speech. He hoped that the representatives of various dioceses across the country and members of the Catholic Action Association would strive to fulfill the mission of the association and create blessings for humanity under the leadership of Archbishop Tsai (the original speech was very long, omitted). Lu Bohong, the chairman of the Catholic Action Association and chairman of the conference, delivered a speech, briefly saying that the National Catholic Action Association is holding a conference today. This conference is of greater significance than ordinary meetings. On the day of the opening of the conference, I would like to thank God for His blessings, which enabled the conference to be successful, and thank Mayor Wu for gracing the meeting with his presence and offering his words of instruction. I have an analogy: When a country is about to go to war with an enemy country, it must summon all the generals of the country to plan the strategies of attack and defense, and then launch an attack to defeat the enemy and win the victory. Today's conference is the same. Engaging in various national education, charity, and social undertakings in the future depends on the planning of the representatives present today, and then we can achieve success in one fell swoop. Finally, I bless you all. At the end, Supervisor Yu Bin reported on the congratulatory telegrams and messages from various parties. The meeting adjourned with music at exactly twelve o'clock.

Donating 20,000 Yuan to Relief Water Disaster

From 3:00 PM, the Proposal Review Committee continued to meet. A total of twenty-three proposals were discussed, all related to the organizational issues of the Catholic Action Association. The meeting adjourned around 4:00 PM. At 5:00 PM, a lecture meeting was held in the Zhengxiu auditorium. After Archbishop Tsai Ning led the recitation of scriptures, Chairman Lu Bohong reported that he had received congratulatory telegrams from various parties in the afternoon. He also announced that the Catholic Church had decided to donate 20,000 yuan to relief the water disaster and asked the bishops, priests, representatives, etc., present to work hard to assist in this righteous act. Then, Bishop Hui of the Shanghai area gave a lecture on "What the Holy Church Hopes from Catholic Action Members," presenting four points for discussion: (1) What is the apostolic work of the Holy Church, and what is the cooperation between Catholic Action members and the clergy in apostolic work? (2) What are the foundations and nature of this vocation of cooperation with the clergy? (3) What are the methods to fully respond to this vocation? Bishop Cheng of Hongtong District spoke on "The Evolution of the Chinese Catholic Action Association," dividing the entire speech into (1) the initial period, (2) the flourishing period, (3) the declining period, and (4) the revival period. The lecture was completed at 7:00 PM. Before the adjournment, Yu Ming reported that, following Archbishop Tsai's intention, the grand dinner at 7:30 PM was canceled and the funds were used to help the water disaster relief, which was unanimously approved by the meeting. Today is the second day of the conference, and the meeting will continue according to the predetermined order.

This City Fortunate to Escape Hurricane; Coastal Areas of Lu and Ji Provinces Inevitably Suffer Wind Disaster; Shanghai Export Ships Sail as Usual 86

The hurricane that originated in the South Pacific on the second of this month has been moving in a northwesterly direction for days. On the seventh, it approached the port of Shanghai. The Meteorological Observatory on the Bund specially hoisted a wind ball to remind the maritime community to pay attention. According to the report from the Observatory, at 6:00 AM on the eighth, the hurricane had reached the ocean surface at 125 degrees 30 minutes east longitude and 32 degrees 30 minutes north latitude, continuing to move northwest. The center of the hurricane was still sixty nautical miles, and the wind force was strong, between eight and nine. According to the above-mentioned position, it was about two hundred and forty nautical miles northeast of the port of Shanghai. This city could avoid being hit by the hurricane. According to the current blowing direction, the coastal areas of Lu and Ji provinces will inevitably suffer from the wind disaster. When the hurricane passed outside Songkou, its left wing scattered. From the evening of the seventh to noon on the eighth, the port experienced gusts of wind and the weather was cool.

The Taikoo Company's Beiyang-class Tongzhou ship had already exported yesterday morning, but the imported ships were all delayed. The Great Britain Company's Ratchiputana, and the Changxing Company's Empress of Japan, were scheduled to arrive at the port yesterday morning but did not arrive until after 3:00 PM. However, the Hengbin Company's Imuran, the Taikoo Yangtze River ship Xiangtan, the Beiyang-class Shuntian, the Nanhua Taiyuan, the China Merchants Nanhua-class Haiyuan, the Jardine Matheson Nanhua-class Yisheng, and the Beiyang Dingsheng, etc., had not yet been reported to customs as of 5:00 PM. They are expected to arrive tonight or tomorrow morning.

Liujiang Coal Mine Company Held Shareholders Meeting Yesterday; Intends to Resolve Judicially or Formally Transfer; Full Authority Granted to Board of Directors for Handling 87

For the matter of the Liujiang Coal Mine Company's mines being forcibly occupied by the Taiji Company, the company held its second extraordinary shareholders meeting at its Shanghai office at 2:00 PM yesterday. More than one hundred and twenty shareholders attended including Li Shuzhen, Liu Hongsheng, Wang Yiting, Zhu Yicai, Shen Shuwen, Yang Kuihou, and Zhu Yinjiang, representing 7,421 shares of capital stock. Li Shuzhen was publicly elected as interim chairman. First, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, briefly stating that the company's mines have now been occupied by Taiji. They have sent letters before and after, intending to buy them all for 300,000 cash. The board of directors considered the matter to be of great importance and convened an extraordinary shareholders meeting to discuss everything. Then, the discussion began. As a result, two proposed solutions were agreed upon: (1) Conduct a judicial resolution, file a lawsuit in the Hebei court against Sun Xianxi, the Chinese registrant of the Taiji Company, and on the other hand, file a complaint with the Japanese Consulate in Tianjin against the Taiji Company, arguing with reason; (2) proceed with the transfer of the mine assets, but on the principle of not harming national sovereignty and the interests of shareholders. The shareholders' meeting granted the board of directors full authority to handle the above two points. The meeting then adjourned.

Forbes' Impressions of China's Industrial, Commercial and Economic Situation: Results of the Economic Survey Mission's Investigation in China; The United States Should Actively Cooperate and Fully Invest 94

Central News Agency: After the return of the American Far East Economic Survey Mission, the National Foreign Trade Council hosted a banquet on July 16 to welcome Shi Zhaoji, China's ambassador to the United States, and Saito, the Japanese ambassador to the United States, who were both invited to attend. During the banquet, Forbes delivered the following speech: Mr. Chairman, Ambassador Saito, Ambassador Shi, and Gentlemen, I am honored to be invited this evening, and I am grateful for the kind words I have heard. On behalf of all members of the survey mission, I would like to express my deepest gratitude. Regarding the economic survey mission's

Achievements in the East: I would like to present a general report, and I hope to receive your guidance. The mission consisted of fifteen members and departed on February 22nd, arrived in Japan on April 4th, departed Japan on April 18th, and proceeded to China. Arrived in Shanghai on April 26th, traveled extensively, returned to the country on June 18th, and arrived in Honolulu on July 3rd. During the journey, the members held frequent meetings and discussions. Upon returning to the country, they also held several consultations and largely determined the materials to be adopted in the report. The members were able to work diligently, and their

Spirit of Harmony and Cooperation: Is especially appreciated by myself. The survey mission received extremely grand hospitality in Japan and China. Local industrial, commercial, and financial leaders prepared comprehensive arrangements and provided diligent guidance. They also had the opportunity to meet with the highest-ranking officials of China and Japan. In Japan, the members met with the Prime Minister, Foreign Minister, and other cabinet members. In China, they met with the President of the Executive Yuan, the Minister of Finance, and other officials, and held important meetings with Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission. I, as the head of the mission, had the honor of meeting with the Emperor of Japan and the Chairman of the National Government of China, which I deeply cherish. During the survey, the members exchanged opinions with the welcoming hosts from China and Japan,

Exchanged Opinions: In addition to enjoying lavish banquets. The members were able to visit factories everywhere without any concealment, setting an unprecedented example. They were able to gain a complete understanding of cost calculations, working methods, and so on. At the same time, the statistical reports prepared by the governments of both countries were also very helpful. In short, the welcome and assistance received during this trip to the East are a matter of great honor for all involved. Furthermore, during the meetings between the mission and the leaders of both countries, both sides were able to be open and honest with each other and discuss ways to promote free trade in a spirit of friendship. First, they sought to identify the difficulties and then frankly stated the opinions of both countries as a basis for drafting concrete suggestions. In both Japan and China, the speeches of the leaders, whether representing the government or industry and commerce, emphasized the close friendship between Japan and the United States or between China and the United States. Here, I must reiterate that this survey mission has absolutely no political implications and is completely unrelated to political events. Sometimes, when politics and economics are intertwined to the point of being inseparable, the mission's concern remains with its

Economic Aspects: Its political aspects are left to the diplomatic personnel to handle. In addition, there is one point that I have repeatedly pointed out: This mission is purely an investigative body and has no executive power. During its stay in Japan and China, visitors often assumed that the mission had come to the Far East to conduct transactions with the industrial and commercial sectors, negotiate prices, and even enter into contracts. In fact, the mission's task was merely to investigate the situation and report it to the people of our country. Whether they sympathize with it or not is not something the survey mission can guarantee. The mission's investigation in Japan was shorter than that in China. However, this does not mean that Japanese-American trade is less important than Chinese-American trade. In 1934, Japanese-American trade totaled $329,671,242, while Chinese-American trade in the same year was $112,564,381, approximately one-third of Japanese-American trade. However, we all know that China's economic development is far behind Japan's. Therefore, there are opportunities in China that cannot be found in Japan. For example, Japan no longer needs foreign capital to develop its various public works, such as railways, steamships, aviation, and other transportation

Such as telephones and telegraphs, etc., while China has excellent opportunities in these areas. The Chinese government currently needs more roads, ships, and other means of land, sea, and air transportation. However, due to a lack of capital, it has not been able to undertake these projects one by one. Under certain circumstances, it should be able to

Welcome Foreign Investment: Furthermore, China's industrial development is far behind Japan's. Therefore, there are many opportunities for the United States to cooperate with China to create the foundation for some industries. Japan, on the other hand, must continue its existing industries and does not need to create new ones. Its need for cooperation with other countries seems to be limited to the supply of fuel oil and gasoline. The mission has already held several discussions with leaders of that country on this issue. However, the main problem in Japan is the recent development of the textile industry. The country's textile industry is now in a severe situation. Previously, Japan's largest source of income from exports was silk exports to the United States. In recent years, due to various reasons, especially the impact of the economic downturn, the amount of silk needed by the United States has been decreasing daily, while at the same time, the price of silk has also fallen sharply. The value of silk currently exported from Japan to the United States has fallen by 60% compared to before, while the tonnage of silk exports has only decreased by 20%. Our government has recently increased taxes on domestic raw material production, so

The Value of Raw Cotton: Has greatly increased. Cotton is a major American export to Japan. Due to the increase in value, Japan's import surplus has increased sharply. The Japanese authorities consider this a very serious problem. The survey mission deeply feels that Japan will soon seek other raw materials to replace American cotton, and our largest export of raw cotton is about to lose its main market. China is currently experimenting with improving cotton varieties, and Brazil also has a large area that can be used for cotton production. Perhaps we will see that when we unwisely raise the value of our products to the point where they cannot compete with other countries, the importing country will inevitably take self-defense measures and seek the same supply elsewhere. The victim will be here rather than there. This is truly something to think deeply about. Japan is now planning to have a total of 10 million spindles by the end of this year, specializing in the weaving of cotton fabrics, which is approximately 1 million more spindles than last year. It is expected that there will be a similar increase in the coming year. The members of the mission exchanged important opinions with the Spinning Association in Osaka several times and visited various factories. The members of the mission suggested to Japan that it should not dump too many goods on the American market at too low a price. If it does, the United States will inevitably be forced to adopt protectionist policies. Although this is quite difficult to manage, we believe that Japan is also aware of this and may take concrete

Remedial Measures: Japanese workers' wages are only one-tenth of those of our country's workers. The cost of production is low, so its capital organization is more economical. The output of each spindle is also greater. Although the wages of its workers are not high and the working hours are long, they are all healthy and happy. During the trip, the survey mission was amazed by the rapid rise of factories along the railways, and the smoke billowing from their chimneys showed how busy they were. After the survey mission completed its investigation in Japan, it proceeded to China. The situation in China is completely different from that in Japan, and the problems are also very different. Most of the suggestions involve American investment in China. Several of China's undertakings require a solid financial foundation, and it is hoped that American capital can join in cooperation, especially since the commercial credit system has much room for development. Given China's current situation, it is unable to do so. Although the United States is China's best customer, American businessmen in China face many difficulties. In Shanghai, in particular, both American and Chinese residents are pessimistic. During its stay in China, the survey mission was advised that Shanghai does not represent all of China and that the financial decline in Shanghai is not enough to indicate that the entire country is similarly affected. In fact, Shanghai is currently experiencing the adverse effects of a real estate boom turning into a bust. Shanghai real estate prices had reached unimaginably high levels. Its rise was rapid, so its decline was also sudden. Before the U.S. government's silver purchase policy affected Chinese commerce, the real estate industry had already reacted. Two or three years ago, when the Red Bandits were rampant in neighboring provinces, Chinese people with property bought and carried their assets to Shanghai for safekeeping. After order was largely restored in the interior, many of the deposits in Shanghai banks were withdrawn to restore industry in the interior. When silver deposits in Shanghai flowed back to the interior, they were simultaneously affected by the U.S. silver policy, leading to exhaustion and difficulty in supporting it. However, there are many thriving scenes in various places in the interior. For example, the increase in railway revenue is one indication. However, Shanghai is ultimately the financial center of the country. During its stay in China, the survey mission heard repeated claims from the Chinese side about the serious impact of the U.S. silver purchase policy on Chinese finance. Now, the United States and several other countries have reduced the value of their currencies in order to promote their trade. The United States has even reduced the value of the gold dollar to 59%. The result of the United States increasing the price of silver has been to increase the value of Chinese silver coins by almost double. When the survey mission exchanged opinions with Chinese financiers, they unanimously believed that this matter

Had a Significant Impact: On China and greatly reduced its trade. These Chinese merchants, who blame the difficulties in Chinese commerce on the

Silver Purchase Policy: Naturally admit more than the survey mission can after investigation. As for the basic and important reason, it is actually that banks, real estate companies, and merchants engaged in real estate have been affected by the drop in land prices, making it difficult for them to recover. However, the silver policy came at the right time, causing Chinese commerce and trade to suffer greatly. If the price of silver had been fixed, commercial failure could have been avoided, but at this time there was no way to escape it. This is absolutely certain. The survey mission also heard from the Chinese side that what most affects Chinese trade is not the price of silver, but the volatility in the value of the currency. If the value of silver coins were fixed and unchanging, then no matter what its value, transactions would be more active. Otherwise, the exchange rate will rise and fall from time to time, and there will be no certainty of profit or loss. It is appropriate that transactions are not prosperous. The survey mission also heard that American commerce in China has recently been greatly affected by various government legislations. Recently, the American courts issued an interpretation of the law determining commercial interest rates that has affected American merchants in China. That is, the interest rate stipulated by American merchants in Shanghai should be the same as that stipulated in the District of Columbia in the United States, so that in certain circumstances, American merchants are unable to obtain cash. In addition, the extension of the American Recovery Act to American merchants in Shanghai has increased the burden, and the result is sufficient to cause American merchants to register with the British government, resulting in American personnel and a British board of directors and British managers. It is obvious that this directly harms American commerce. China is now sweeping the remnants of bandits to remote areas, still to be cleared. In addition, the influence of Soviet Russia in Mongolia and Japan in the provinces adjacent to Manchuria is sufficient to reduce the extent to which the central government manages its territory. In

Currency System: Although China has the silver dollar as its national currency, the national currency system has not yet been unified. The value of banknotes in Guangdong, Sichuan, Tianjin, and Shanghai is different, and their exchange rate fluctuates from time to time, and it is also inconsistent with the two yuan in Hong Kong. Chinese exporters still mix low-quality goods with high-quality goods. This suicidal trick is enough to reduce China's reputation in the world market and cause customers to seek goods from other merchants, such as the United States' purchase of tung oil, which is one example. The current government is trying to crack down on this bad habit, and the results should be considerable. The biggest problem that China needs to remedy is the smuggling of goods. However, under the current circumstances, China is unable to fully control tax revenue, which is greatly affected. The so-called treaty ports will also be merely a name, because smuggled goods are rampant and prices are naturally low. It is difficult for legitimate goods to gain a foothold. To reduce this problem, we should

Cooperate with Other Countries to Strictly Enforce Anti-Smuggling: In short, the United States is a good place to invest in China. The obstacles to Sino-American trade are very small. What we should always pay attention to is the opportunity for trade with China. Even if there are difficulties, they are only technical. If they can be eliminated, the future is unlimited. The two countries do not need to compete with each other in terms of natural resources, production, or even needs. The places where they complement each other are many. A country that produces silk clothes and cotton trades with a country that produces cotton clothes and silk. The extremely developed industry of the United States trades with the luxury goods made by Chinese handicrafts. The two countries have the natural resources they need and have a large population to guarantee long-term needs. The good opportunities for the future are probably better than any other market. During its stay in China, the survey mission received many useful suggestions to develop American trade. The efforts of the Chinese authorities in unification should be assisted by all friends of China and friends of world culture. As a result of the survey, the survey mission deeply feels that China has reached a level in this process of reform (or rebirth) that the United States should actively cooperate and fully invest in. China now needs full financial assistance to promote its efforts, such as railways, such as shipping, such as airplanes, such as the opening of ports, such as the excavation of mines, such as the construction of factories, etc. If measures can be taken properly, the progress of the new China into a strong and prosperous country will be so rapid that it will shock the whole world.

According to the radio station of the airplane, it will arrive in Guangzhou at about 3:00 PM on the 8th. The total distance from Berlin to Shanghai is 15,200 kilometers. This is only the second time to fly directly from Germany to China, so it is very important for Eurasia air traffic.

Flying to Shanghai This Morning

After the giant airplane arrived in Guangzhou yesterday, it stayed there overnight. A Glimpse of the Structure

According to the Eurasia Aviation Corporation, the structure of the airplane is as follows: The airplane is the latest type of large airplane in Germany, equipped with three engines, each with 550 to 700 horsepower. The speed is extremely fast, and the ability to rise and fall is also very agile. In addition to the wireless radio, all new instruments are available, and it can also fly in poisonous fog. Its maximum speed is 290 kilometers per hour, and the normal flying speed is 260 kilometers per hour. The carrying capacity is 9,200 kilograms. All equipment in the airplane is very suitable for the special conditions of the Eastern airline. In addition to carrying between 14 and 16 passengers, there is also a cargo bay. The weight of the mail and goods carried is equal to the weight of the passengers carried. The cargo hold is in the rear of the airplane and is equipped with washrooms, coat racks, luggage racks, and other facilities. It is very beautiful.

Representatives of Oilcake Factories and Transportation Merchants Returned to Shanghai from Beijing Yesterday; Mr. Gu Xinyi Talked About the Successful Results of the Petition 101

Representatives of the oilcake and grain merchants, including Gu Xinyi, returned to Shanghai by overnight train the night before, arriving at 7:15 AM yesterday. According to Mr. Gu's conversation with the reporter of Dagong News Agency, the central authorities stated that they would approve a telegram to Guangdong to stop the collection of surcharges on bran in Guangdong Province, and the Executive Yuan will convene a meeting of the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry to discuss the matter. The details are as follows:

Returned to Shanghai Yesterday Morning

The oilcake, miscellaneous grain, and transportation merchants dispatched Gu Xinyi, Chen Ziyi, Jiang Hongbin, Cao Xingeng, He Quesheng, He Zisheng, Xie Boqin, and other seven representatives to form a petition group, together with Mr. Zheng Zenan, the supervisor of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and traveled to Beijing on the evening of the 5th to petition various ministries and commissions of the central government. The results were satisfactory. After the representatives completed their petition in Beijing, they returned to Shanghai by the 11:00 PM express train the night before, arriving at the port at 7:15 AM yesterday and returned to their residences to rest.

Central Consultation

After arriving in Beijing on the morning of the 6th, the petition representatives went to the Legislative Yuan to petition. They were received by Director Chen, the Ministry of Finance was received by Mr. Gao Bingfang, the Director of the Tax Department, the Ministry of Industry was received by Mr. Liang Shangdong, the Director of the Commerce Department, and the Executive Yuan was received by Mr. Peng Xuepei, the Deputy Minister of Political Affairs. Each department accepted the petition request regarding the collection of bran surcharges in Guangdong Province and stopped it. The Ministry of Finance also immediately telegraphed the Guangdong side to exempt it. The Executive Yuan plans to convene a meeting of the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry to discuss disposal methods in the coming days.

Mr. Gu's Talk

At 10:00 AM, a reporter from the Dagong News Agency visited Mr. Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Oilcake and Miscellaneous Grain Association, at Yongda Rice Bank and asked about the process of the petition in Beijing. According to him, the central authorities believe that at the time when harsh taxes and miscellaneous donations are being abolished to alleviate the people's difficulties, there should be no further collection of this bran surcharge. Moreover, bran is a fertilizer for sugarcane farmers, which will inevitably increase the burden on farmers. Therefore, the Guangdong authorities were telegraphed to exempt it. The reporter also asked when he would leave to petition in Guangdong Province again. He said that he would convene a meeting to report the situation of the central government before making a decision.

Meeting This Afternoon

The Oil Mill Industry Association, the Miscellaneous Grain and Oilcake Industry Association, and the transportation merchants of various oil mills in Shanghai, Xichang, Kunshan, Hubei, Guangdong, etc., will hold a plenary meeting at 3:00 PM today to hear the petition representatives' report on the petition in Beijing and discuss continuing to go to Guangdong Province to petition the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, the Financial Commissioner's Office, and other agencies to request the abolition of shop donations.

上海縣禁烟會議 104

The Shanghai County Anti-Smoking Committee held its 21st meeting yesterday. Chairman Ye Zhendong discussed and resolved the following cases: (1) Ratify the committee's routine expenses expenditure, investigate and prepare the budget, and submit it to the province for approval; (2) Approve the budget for the anti-smoking center, selectively adding medicines and sundries, and submit it to the province for approval; (5) Grant retention of the anti-smoking center director Qian Huilun's request to resign. In addition, a temporary motion was made regarding how to strictly supervise the county's three-year deadline for banning smoking to ensure its completion on schedule. The resolutions were: (1) Refer to the methods passed by the 19th meeting of this committee. For repeat smokers, in addition to being sentenced to imprisonment according to law, they will also be paraded in the streets to warn others; (2) Schedule a meeting of district chiefs and directors and patrol officers of public security bureaus to implement the use of Baojia to investigate and squeeze out smokers; (5) Smokers who quit smoking should be guaranteed by the Baojia head where they are located; (4) For smokers who quit smoking, if temporary investigations reveal relapse, the Baojia head should report to the nearest public security bureau for detention and interrogation; if they know and do not report, the Baojia head must be jointly and severally responsible; (5) Schedule a notice to smokers who quit smoking to gather in public places in districts, and the committee will assign doctors to go and check whether they have relapsed, and send personnel to give speeches on the harms of opium.

商檢局檢騐植物　發現顯著病害　計有綠徵病灰斑病等 108

According to Guomin News Agency, since the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau implemented plant pest inspection, it has found a large number of significant diseases in imported and exported goods. For example, green speck disease on pears, yellow pears, apples, pomelos, oranges, lemons, etc. The origin of these fruits is Yokohama, Japan, the United States, and Yantai, Shandong. Next is brown spot disease on eggplants, which originates from Hong Kong and Guangdong. Scab disease, black scurf, and charcoal rot disease on potatoes originate from Nanjing, Shanghai, and California. Other diseases include fruit rot on apples, which originates from Nagasaki, Japan, and gray spot disease on loquats, which originates from Japan. The Commodity Inspection Bureau refuses to import or appropriately handles all items found with diseases.

納稅會請工部局　嚴懲汽車司機肇禍　希望工部局秉公辦理無間國籍 116

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association believes that the Public Concession Police always favors the driver in car accidents. Recently, in the cases of private car No. 10099 damaging the medicine delivery car of Tongchuntang Chinese Medicine Store and car No. 1797 reversing carelessly and injuring the girl Sun Yuexiang, the handling was particularly unfair. Yesterday, they sent separate letters to the Public Works Department and the Ningbo Association in Shanghai. The original letters are recorded below:

Damaged Medicine Car

The Ratepayers Association wrote to the Public Works Department: To whom it may concern, we received a letter from the First District Branch of the Shanghai City No. 1 Special Zone Citizens' Union, stating, "Our member store, Tongchuntang Chinese Medicine Store, stated in a letter that our No. 3 medicine delivery car was driving on the east side of Hankou Road and Hubei Road at 5:20 pm on September 1st when a private car No. 10099, without following the driving regulations, drove too fast and tried to overtake the car in front, causing the rear wheel of the car to be damaged. The person in the car almost fell. Fortunately, our driver had good driving experience and was not in any danger. At that time, the patrol officer on duty and the driver of the car and medicine car went to the police car office to discuss the matter, but the car office handled it vaguely and refused to accept it, only instructing them to directly claim compensation from the car owner. "We believe that Shanghai is a densely populated city with heavy traffic. If the vehicles do not follow the regulations, the danger is unimaginable. Therefore, before an accident occurs, we rely on the patrol officers who manage the traffic to give good instructions. After the accident occurs, we rely on the car office to handle it seriously. This time, our medicine car was damaged by car No. 10099 violating the regulations, but the car office handled it casually, which is very inappropriate. We should ask your association to forward a letter to the Public Works Department to strictly order the police to detain and severely punish those who violate traffic regulations in the future, so that drivers dare not neglect and reduce the danger. "We have learned that Shanghai is a large commercial port with a large population and many vehicles and pedestrians. The command and management of traffic are extremely important. If an accident occurs, the responsible person should file a public lawsuit and severely punish the person who caused the accident to warn others in the future. Now the police ignore it, which is really inappropriate. According to the letter, we hereby consult your association and ask you to inform the Public Works Department to investigate and handle it according to the circumstances." Because of the previous letter, we should consult your association and ask you to inform the Public Works Department to investigate and handle it according to the circumstances." The above-mentioned situation has often occurred. Your bureau stated in a letter to our association on August 27 that "if there is sufficient evidence to file a public lawsuit, the police will pay attention to it, regardless of nationality." The rear of the medicine car was destroyed (and recently, Zhang Yuexiang was injured and lying next to the rear wheel of the car, and the physical evidence was there, but no public lawsuit was filed, and the court made a fair trial). Instead, they made their own decisions and allowed the perpetrators to not bear the responsibility. It is appropriate that the British Public Bus (No. 10,150) ran over and killed a six-year-old boy named Li Ruizhang from Guangdong on Seward Road. If you want the public to know that there is no bias, then the facts speak louder than words. Due to the previous letter, we hereby request your bureau to investigate and handle it promptly.

Reversing Injured Child

The Ratepayers Association also wrote to the Public Works Department: To whom it may concern, we received a letter from the Ningbo Association in Shanghai, stating that "our association member Sun Hongfu, who lives at 816 Zhangjiazhaikou, Wenyilu, stated that at 6:00 pm on June 24th, his daughter Yuexiang, who is ten years old, was playing in the alley behind the house when a Westerner suddenly drove a car (No. 1797) into the alley. Yuexiang was run over and injured her leg. The member reported the incident to our association, which sent a letter to the General Patrol Room. After the Traffic Office, we received a reply from the office on June 29th, stating that the owner of car No. 1797 was Eddie S. Taylor, who lived at the International Hotel and whose office was at No. 150 Jiujiang Road. At that time, the news police claimed that they had obtained permission from the Chinese doorman to reverse into Zhangjiazhaikou from Wenyilu. Suddenly, they heard a cry and immediately stopped the car. They saw that the injured child was lying under the rear left wheel. Since no road police witnessed the accident, there was no clear evidence to prove the driver's negligence, so this office could not file a lawsuit. "We immediately informed the victim's family, who replied that the alley did not have a Chinese doorman. After the accident, Mr. Chen Yongkang, the manager of the Minhua Printing Factory, called the New Gate Police Station, who came to rescue. At that time, the car driven by Ai Wenyilu turned east into Zhangjiazhaikou Road and did not honk the horn. It reversed straight into the alley of Youhua Automobile Company on Zhangjiazhaikou Road, causing the corner of the wall to be damaged and affecting the little girl. There are neighbors who can testify. Attached are a photo and diagram of the damaged corner of the wall. Please provide assistance and ask the police station to file a public lawsuit. "We sent a letter to the General Patrol Room of the Public Concession in the middle of last month with a photo and diagram of the corner of the wall that was damaged, requesting investigation and handling, but the police station has not replied to our association about the handling of the case. The family claimed that although the little girl Yuexiang had been discharged from the hospital a few days ago, she still had a fever and her injured leg was more than an inch shorter, making her disabled. The police station ignored the case, which was obviously protecting the driver. Please ask us to continue to negotiate. "Based on this, the driver's negligence was obvious, and the police station ignored it, which was obviously protecting the driver. According to the previous situation, we urgently ask your association to review and approve it and promptly send a letter to the General Patrol Room for thorough investigation and handling to calm public anger and maintain humanity. "The association has learned that car accidents should be handled equally regardless of nationality, without discrimination, in order to meet the public's expectations. However, your bureau imposed legal sanctions on Chinese people who caused car accidents and filed public lawsuits in court. For car accidents caused by British China Public Motors, it often claimed that there was no evidence and allowed them to remain at large. However, because the person in charge of the company was powerful, it was reluctant to act against them, which was not in accordance with the law but was excusable in the circumstances. As for the perpetrator in this case, it also used the lack of clear evidence to shirk its responsibility to file a public lawsuit and disregarded the witnesses provided by the victim's family. We don't know what the reason is. This association believes that it is a great regret. Based on the previous letter, we hereby request your bureau to act in accordance with the law promptly so that the competent court can make a fair judgment and maintain the position of the public authority.

Letter to Ningbo Association

The Ratepayers Association also sent a letter to the Ningbo Association in Shanghai: "To whom it may concern, we received a reply from the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Public Concession, stating, 'Regarding your letter of August 7th about the car accident on the corner of Ai Wenyilu and Zhangjiazhaikou Road on June 24th, when the board of directors investigated, the driver of car No. 1797 was Adam Stotler, a Swede residing at the International Hotel. At that time, Chang Mou, who was a member of the Youhua Automobile Company at the intersection of Zhangjiazhaikou Road, indicated to driver Stotler that there were no pedestrians on the road. However, after Mr. Si drove the car, he reversed about nine feet and suddenly heard a scream. He immediately stopped the car and checked. He saw Zhang Yuexiang lying on the ground near the rear wheel of the car. Mr. Si immediately informed the police station to conduct an investigation. However, after the investigation, there were no witnesses on the scene. The car employer and your letter stated that the residents nearby had been questioned and all said that they had not seen it. They only came out to help after hearing Zhang Yuexiang's scream. In this way, if we want to file a public lawsuit, the evidence is insufficient. Therefore, the police did not take any action. The last paragraph of your letter is unfounded. Those who have sufficient evidence can file a public lawsuit, and the police will pay attention to it regardless of nationality. This is a well-known fact. 'We should check and act accordingly. "This is addressed to the Ningbo Association in Shanghai.
