A Married Man Lures Away a Young Girl; Zhou Xiaomei is Hidden; Yao Fuyu is Seized by the Girl's Mother; Detectives Arrest Him and Send Him to the Authorities for Prosecution 118

Zhou Xiaomei, a girl from Gaoyou, is nineteen years old, beautiful and charming. She lives on Huasheng Road. Recently, she became romantically involved with Yao Fuyu (24 years old), a fellow townsman and motor mechanic at Yihe Cotton Mill. They went to the Tangshan Inn on Tangshan Road several times to rent rooms to sleep together. Her mother, Zhou Ma, was initially unaware of this. Later, she found out and negotiated with Yao, but to no avail. On the evening of the 17th of last month, when the girl went out to watch a Taoist ritual, she was lured away by Yao and disappeared without a trace. Her mother asked people everywhere for help, but received no information. The next morning, she reported the matter to the Yulin Road police station, which sent detectives to investigate. There were no clues to be found. It wasn't until the day before yesterday that she learned of Yao's workplace. At 6:00 p.m. that afternoon, when the factory finished work, she waited nearby and indeed saw Yao come out. She then grabbed him, demanding that he hand over her daughter, Xiaomei. Yao, in desperation, used force to throw her to the ground and cried for help. Hua, policeman number 723, and detective Zhao Jianchun arrived at the scene after hearing the alarm. They arrested Yao and, after questioning him, learned that Zhou Xiaomei was hidden in the pavilion building at No. 45, Xinkang Lane, Yangzhou Road. They went there, rescued the girl, and handed her back to her mother. Yao was taken to the Yulin Road police station for detention. Yesterday, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, filed a public prosecution against him for crimes such as disrupting the family under Article 240, Section 13 of the Criminal Law, stating that the defendant already has a wife and children and should not have engaged in such unlawful acts. Under questioning, the defendant confessed that in June of this year, he met Zhou at a certain theater on Huasheng Road. They talked to each other and became acquainted. On July 17th, he met her again at the theater, and she agreed to stay at the Tangshan Inn. This happened about twice. On the 17th of last month, the girl voluntarily rented a house in Xinkang Lane to live in. At that time, she made it clear that she had a wife, and she was willing to be a concubine. On the 28th, the girl went to a fortune-telling stall to write a letter to her family. Moreover, her mother invited many people to a certain teahouse, saying that she had to pay 100 yuan to marry the girl to me as a concubine, etc. According to Zhou Xiaomei, she is eighteen years old and not yet married. She had physical relations with the defendant, first at his house and then at the Tangshan Inn. At that time, he claimed to be unmarried. It wasn't until they lived together in Xinkang Lane that he said he had a principal wife and wanted her to be a concubine, etc. Zhou Ma stated the process of her daughter's abduction and denied the matter of asking him to pay 100 yuan to marry the girl as a concubine. After reviewing the statements, Judge Wang ordered Yao Fuyu to be detained and scheduled a sentencing date.

A Woman in Labor Falls and Dies; In-Laws Falsely Accuse Her Husband's Parents of Abuse; Court Examination Proves Death Due to Illness; Yang Guoshun and Others Still Seek Other Plans 119

Chen Longshan, from Jingjiang, is over sixty years old. He runs a Chen Shengtai paper goods and incense store at No. 99, 101, and 121 Kangti Road (corner of the vegetable market) in the French Concession, as a sole proprietorship. In his early years, he had the sorrow of not having a son, so he adopted one named Chen Donglin. This year, at the age of twenty-one, through a matchmaker, he married the only daughter of Yang Guoshun and Yang Pei (currently residing at No. 6, Qingyun Lane, Xinqiao Road, Nanshi, in the Chinese area), named Yang (the same age as Chen Donglin), as his daughter-in-law. Chen's family, including his son and daughter-in-law, lived together in the store. Yang has been pregnant for over a month now, past her due date. At around 5:00 p.m. on the 6th, Yang was sitting on a chair in her room upstairs when she suddenly fell to the ground and couldn't get up. At that time, her father-in-law was out at a money exchange shop to exchange silver dollars, and her mother-in-law had gone to the home of a fellow townsman in Anshun Lane, Kangti Road, to collect membership fees. Therefore, no one noticed when Yang fell. Chen Longshan was downstairs in the store and did not hear the noise upstairs, so he was completely unaware. Dai Shilong, the owner of the Dai Wanxing sesame cake and porridge shop across the street, went upstairs and, seeing through the window, notified Chen Longshan. Chen Longshan immediately called neighbors to go upstairs, helped Yang up, and recognized that she was about to give birth. He immediately called a midwife and others to prepare everything. However, she did not give birth and was shaking uncontrollably. He immediately sent someone to notify her parents, Yang Guoshun and Yang Pei, who rushed over. However, they were unable to help and instead claimed that she had been beaten. Her father-in-law wanted to send her to the hospital, but her parents stopped him. Chen Longshan reported the matter to the French Concession police station. After repeated delays, she was finally sent to the Ximen Women and Children's Hospital at 1:00 a.m. that night. After examination, Doctor Yi Le'ai determined that Chen Yang was suffering from pre-eclampsia. Because it had been too long since it occurred, there was no way to save her. At 6:00 a.m. the next morning, she was carried back home, and she died an hour later. Afterwards, the deceased's parents filed a complaint with the procuratorate of the Second Special District Court and reported to the French police that their daughter had been beaten and abused by her husband's parents, resulting in her unexplained death, requesting redress. Meanwhile, they argued incessantly at the deceased's home. The deceased's father-in-law also reported to the police that the deceased's parents were trying to extort money by using the corpse. The police ordered the corpse to be sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall for examination. That day, they reported to the Second Special District Court, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with a forensic doctor and clerk, to conduct a detailed examination of the corpse at the hall according to the law, and to sit in public hearing of the case. The corpse's father, Yang Guoshun, repeatedly kowtowed, claiming that he wanted to seek justice, but could not say the reason for the abuse and injuries inflicted on her by her husband's parents. Yang Pei stated that after she got the news and rushed to inquire about her daughter, she only said one sentence: "Dear mother, please seek justice for me," and then could not speak. She said that usually, her mother-in-law would often scold her for not washing clothes cleanly and often beat her. Yesterday, her daughter was sitting on a stool when her mother-in-law pushed her to the ground. When asked for evidence, Pei was speechless. Finally, the corpse's father-in-law, Chen Longshan, stated that the deceased was his daughter-in-law. After she fell yesterday, he wanted to send her to the hospital, but her parents refused to let him. After several pleadings, they were unreasonable and instead quarreled incessantly. Many people witnessed the quarrel and can testify to the fact that the death of his daughter-in-law was caused by her parents preventing her from being sent to the hospital in time. After reviewing the statements, Prosecutor Wang determined that Chen Yang died of illness. The corpse was handed over to Chen Longshan for burial. After the verdict, the corpse's uncle, Yang Guoxing (a shop assistant), along with the corpse's father, proposed to dissect the corpse to clarify the grievance. The official stated that it has already been verified that the deceased died of illness, and there is hospital diagnosis proof of this, so there is no need for dissection. The official ordered the bailiff to wave them out. Yang and others left reluctantly, intending to find another solution to negotiate. After the corpse's father-in-law completed the autopsy, he prepared clothes and a coffin overnight, placed the corpse in it, and kept it in the guild hall, preparing for the deceased's family to resolve the matter legally.

Water Disaster Carnival Closed Yesterday; Meeting This Afternoon to Expedite Closing Matters 120

The Shanghai All Sectors Water Disaster Carnival, previously held at the New World Amusement Park to raise funds through entertainment, has now reached its closing date and ended last night. At 7:00 p.m. last night, the association specially convened representatives from the city's film industry at the Atlantic Restaurant to discuss the matter. The details are recorded as follows:

Film Entertainment Preparations Meeting

Multiple Accidents After the Death of Prominent Pawnshop Merchant; Uncle Forces Nephew to Sign Sales Contract; Concubine Files a Lawsuit Declaring the Contract Invalid; Niece to Demand Partition of Inheritance 123

After Li Pengxian, a prominent pawnshop merchant from Ningbo, died of illness on the 5th day of the second month of the lunar calendar this year, his second son, Yusheng, also passed away on the 27th of the same month. Li Pengxian's estate was entirely managed by his eldest son, Yu Sheng, owner of Yuchang Metal Company. Yu Sheng had a wife, Sun, who gave birth to a daughter, and a concubine, Shi, who gave birth to a son, Cheng Hao, who is not yet an adult. Recently, Yu Sheng sold a portion of the estate, a piece of land on North Meiyuan Road, for a price of 2,800 yuan. When signing the contract, Yu Sheng insisted that Cheng Hao sign it. Afterwards, Cheng Hao's mother, Li Shi Zhongde, claimed that her son's signature at the time was obtained under duress and questioned the sale of the land. She then hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit against Li Yu Sheng in the First Special District Court to confirm the invalidity of the sales contract. There have been several summons and attempts at mediation, but no agreement has been reached to date. Therefore, yesterday, Judge Shen Hong of the First Special District Court continued the hearing in the Sixth Civil Division. Zhou, Li Pengxian's wife, and Sun, Li Yusheng's wife, were summoned to court for questioning. Then, Li Shi stated that she had never been consulted before the sale of the land and that the signature was signed during the period of her late husband's seventh-day memorial, and they took advantage of this opportunity to force her son to sign. Finally, the plaintiff's lawyer and the defendant's lawyer, Wang Chuanbi, argued with each other. Judge Shen then adjourned the hearing for further verification. It is heard that Li Jiaorong, Li Pengxian's married daughter, has also hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Li Yu Sheng and Cheng Hao to demand the partition of her father's estate of 150,000 yuan, requesting to split it into three parts, totaling 50,000 yuan. This case will also be heard by the court in the near future.

Drug Traffickers Wu Fashou and Others Sentenced to Imprisonment; Hua Changsheng and Yao Jisheng Acquitted 124

Detectives Mao Jinsheng, Wang Zhihao, and Bao Zhang Fengming of the French Concession Police Station successively arrested drug traffickers Wu Fashou (35 years old, from Taizhou), Wang Gu (38 years old, from Haimen), Wu Acai (33 years old, from Changshu), and Chang Fukang (nicknamed "Turtle Little Boss," 28 years old, from Yangzhou), as well as suspects Hua Changsheng (32 years old, from Zhenjiang) and Yao Jisheng (29 years old, from Ningbo), at No. 12, Bai'er Road, No. 124, Caishi Road, No. 275, Mintini Yin Road, the overpass in Jinyu Lane, No. 3, Jinyu Lane, and No. 435-5, Ailaige Road on the 16th of last month. A thousand red pills and sixteen small packages of morphine were seized from the homes of Wu Fashou and Chang Fukang. Under questioning, Wu and others confessed that they bought the red pills from "Hankou Asi," the big boss at No. 32, Fuchang Lane, Sixth Road, and the morphine came from a phone call to No. 94248, and someone would deliver the goods. The detectives went to arrest Hankou Asi, but he had already fled after hearing the news. Wu and others were then sent to the Second Special District Court, where the police lawyer filed a public prosecution against them for the crime of selling opium substitutes in violation of the Sixth Amendment to the Anti-Smoking Law. The investigation is detailed in this newspaper. The case has been concluded by Judge Zhang Chaozuo, who sentenced Wu Fashou and Wang Gu to two months of imprisonment each, Wu Acai to one year and six months of imprisonment, and Chang Fukang to four months of imprisonment. The seized red pills and morphine were confiscated and burned. Hua Changsheng and Yao Jisheng were acquitted. After the verdict, the defendants were ordered to be transferred to the detention center during the appeal period.

Liang Tongfang Represents Villagers in an Appeal to the Zhejiang Provincial Government Regarding the Expansion of the Yuan Lake Sluice Gate Damaging Farmland; Requests Order to Rebuild According to the Old Design to Protect Water Conservancy 126

According to the Shiye Society, Liang Tongfang, a patriotic person, was recently requested by 150 fellow villagers, including Liang Jiajin, Liang Guiren, Ni Fucheng, Fu Tuchao, and Wang Abao, to represent all the villagers in an appeal to the Zhejiang Provincial Government regarding the damage to farmland caused by the kiln owner Wang Guoquan expanding the Yuan Lake sluice gate. A reporter from the Shiye Society recorded the details as follows:

Representative Appeal

Liang Tongfang is originally from Shunmu Township, Shangyu County, Zhejiang Province. When he returned to his hometown last month to visit his relatives, more than 150 villagers, including Liang Jiajin, Liang Jiafa, Liang Guiren, Liang Jiazhen, Liang Wufu, Liang Caifu, Fu Shichao, Fu Mengyu, Fu Afang, Fu Fanglian, Wang Abao, Yu Renzhao, Lu Yuting, Zhu Hualin, and Zhu Meijin, stated that the local kiln owner Wang Guoquan was acting in his own interests, damaging the farmland, and had secretly requested the Construction Department to expand the Yuan Lake sluice gate, which is extremely important for farmland water conservancy, to more than double its original size. They were indignant and convened a large farmers' meeting, publicly requesting Liang to act as their full representative and appeal to the provincial government to rebuild the gate to its original width in order to store water and irrigate farmland. It is learned that Liang has already submitted a document to the Zhejiang Provincial Government requesting permission to order the Shangyu County Government to handle the matter.

Petition to the Provincial Government

Petition for the expansion of the sluice gate damaging farmland, a sincere plea for information, respectfully requesting consideration and ordering the Shangyu County Government to allow the restoration to its original state. The petitioners reside in Jiapang Village, Shunmu Township, Shangyu County, Zhejiang Province. There is a Yuan Lake in the area, with an area of approximately eighty mu and a circumference of approximately one li. The land under its protection is approximately eight hundred mu. Since ancient times, a stone sluice gate has been placed on the lake embankment, known as the "Lake Gate," to discharge water into the Tongjing River, which flows directly to the large river. Later, because the gate was in disrepair for many years, the owners and tenants of the protected farmland jointly submitted a request to the county government to construct the lake gate in 1936. Unexpectedly, Wang Guoquan, a nearby kiln owner, clinging to his own interests and disregarding the public good, believed that the gate was too small to allow mud boats to pass through. He dared to come out and resist and obstruct the construction. Fortunately, the former County Magistrate Zhang Jingxu ordered the district bureau chief to stipulate the width of the gate to be four chi and sent police to supervise the construction, which was finally completed. However, Wang Guoquan was dissatisfied and acted arbitrarily, taking advantage of his power to secretly expand the lake gate to more than double its original size that winter in order to facilitate his own purposes. Mud boats can now freely enter and exit, but since then, the lake water cannot be stored, and it quickly dries up in times of drought. The income of the eight hundred mu of farmland under its protection is completely hopeless. The lake is higher than the farmland, and there is no source of water flowing into it. It relies entirely on rainwater to fill it. Moreover, it is not far from the large river, and the water flows downstream unimpeded. Therefore, since ancient times, the lake gate has been built with a width of only a few chi. During the spring plowing, it is necessary to discharge water from time to time and divert it into the Tong River to irrigate the farmland outside the lake. However, it is only opened and closed by officials to provide irrigation. The intention is to prevent the water from overflowing and ensure that every drop goes to the farmland. If the gate is as wide as it is now, the rapid current will quickly recede and drain easily. Recalling the drought last year, the lake dried up before other lakes, and the crops yielded nothing, which serves as a warning. Now, the villagers have entrusted us to continue to appeal. It is in the private interest of the mud boat to have access, while it is in the public interest of the irrigation of the farmland. How can one favor private interests over the public good? And how can one lightly overturn and sacrifice the centuries-old established rules to the misguided notion of satisfying one's own desires? Is this not a strange thing? We believe that our wise government will not allow this to happen. The villagers represented by the petitioners are purely for the public good and have no selfish motives. We have always admired your government's unwavering efforts to revive agriculture and its eagerness to save the people from water and fire. We humbly request that you quickly order the transfer of the instructions issued by former County Magistrate Zhang Jingxu in May 1931, as well as the files related to the supervision of the construction of the Yuan Lake Gate and the petition submitted to County Magistrate Chen for reconstruction in July of this year, for your review and approval. Please also order the Shangyu County Government to allow the restoration to its original state to protect water conservancy and maintain agriculture. We eagerly await your response. Presented to the Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, Huang, by the village representative Liang Tongfang of Shunm Township, Shangyu County.

Recent News from the Silver Industry Resumption Preparatory Office 129

Since the Ningbo Industrial Bank temporarily ceased receiving deposits and withdrawals, for the sake of restoring the commercial reputation of Ningbo people in Shanghai, and to protect the interests of all creditors, the Ningbo natives in Shanghai, along with the bank's directors, supervisors, and creditors, jointly initiated a resumption movement to plan for the bank's resumption. Subsequently, with the consent of all creditors, the signing and subscription for resumption and increased capital reached three-quarters of the total amount of the bank's debts. The handling has shown initial progress, and through repeated newspaper announcements and the election of preparatory members to establish a preparatory office, all work is being conducted openly. It is hoped that members of society will witness this together. On August 3rd, the association received a letter from Commissioner Luo, appointed by the Ministry [of Finance], inquiring about the resumption plan and instructing that the progress of the resumption be reported at any time. The Resumption Movement Association complied with the instructions and, on August 7th, August 16th, and August 24th, submitted to Commissioner Luo the plan for resuming and clearing debts, the names of the initiators, and the amount of resumption capital signed and subscribed by each creditor, respectively, for submission to the Ministry of Finance for approval and record. There were receipts for income and expenditure as proof. Although it is uncertain whether Commissioner Luo has forwarded our submitted documents to the Ministry of Finance, as official approval has not yet been received, we dare not make any predictions. However, Commissioner Luo is already fully aware of all aspects of our handling of the resumption, as evidenced by written records. Yesterday, we saw in the Shanghai newspaper that Commissioner Luo's reply to lawyer Qiu stated that he was not clear about our resumption situation. We cannot fathom the intention behind this. In addition to requesting Commissioner Luo to explain in person, we are deeply concerned about misunderstandings in all sectors. Therefore, we hereby declare the facts of the submission to the Ministry. However, our handling of the resumption is actively progressing. We are doing our utmost to seek benefits for creditors and will not terminate our work due to external misunderstandings.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 138

— (Microorganism)

Lying diagonally in a rented car, laughing at the people walking slowly on the sidewalk, who knew a horse-drawn carriage would pass by your car, and the people in the carriage were also laughing at you for being slow. Friend, don't laugh! The people in trams and automobiles are also laughing at our speed, as none of us are as fast as them! This kind of laughing at each other perfectly matches a common saying: "Sufficient compared to those below, but insufficient compared to those above." The same is true of people's wealth!

You secretly add fuel to the fire in front of your superiors, energetically speaking ill of your colleagues. Like a hairy soybean, you pick the plump pods to attack and crush others. Perhaps after you leave, someone else may be wagging their tongue and kicking their feet in front of your superiors, talking about your "shortcomings," attacking and crushing you!

The Franco-Prussian War and the Rotating Pillar in Front of Barber Shops 139

— Gu Zhangqing

In this publication, Mr. Wu Aibo provided an explanation for the rotating pillar in front of barber shops. He based his account on a traveler's observations, believing it originated in Europe. In ancient Europe, barbers also practiced as surgeons, hence its use as a symbol. This seems quite reasonable, as many barbers in our country also practice as surgeons. However, according to my knowledge, there is another explanation: It is said that during the Franco-Prussian War, a French barber was brave and skilled in battle, single-handedly killing over a hundred enemies, but eventually died. The French authorities praised his loyalty and valor in sacrificing himself for the country, and specially wrapped his body in the red, white, and blue national flag and transported it back to his hometown as a way to honor him. Therefore, barbers adopted this as a matter of pride, and to commemorate the event, they erected such a thing in front of each barber shop, which has been passed down to this day, and is also practiced abroad.

Based on this account, I am writing this down based on memory. Let this be just one explanation. If this symbol already existed before the Franco-Prussian War, or if there are other reasons, I am not insightful and will not investigate further.

Streetlights 140

— Rong Yu

On busy streets, hundreds of bright streetlights stand and connect, illuminating the area as if it were daytime, benefiting vehicles, horses, and pedestrians. Even on quiet roads, a streetlight with a dozen or so lights shines every ten yards or so, allowing pedestrians to see their feet clearly and avoid bumping into things. Who says streetlights are just decorations? In the dark night, they are as effective as a compass in the vast sea.

All things progress with the passage of time, and even these small streetlights have undergone many changes. When I was young, busy streets only had flickering sky lanterns, which were wooden poles with a square glass frame on top, inside which was an oil lamp. Small streets didn't even have this kind of lamp. On clear moonlit nights, walking on the road wasn't too bad; but on dark and windy nights, if you didn't have a candle in your hand, you couldn't see your fingers in front of you, and no matter how capable you were, you couldn't walk on the unfamiliar road. Sometimes dogs would lie in the street, and you would step on one and get bitten. Sometimes pedestrians would come face to face, and everyone would bump into each other fiercely before they could avoid each other. People who have never experienced this would certainly think I'm exaggerating, but if you ask older people, they will certainly say it's true! Later, in Shanghai, oil streetlights were abolished and replaced with gas streetlights, with a glass cover and a gauze shade inside, emitting a green flame. Although they were bright, they were also somewhat eerie. But the interior didn't even have this kind of lamp! It wasn't until electric lights were invented and transmitted to China that streetlights were also upgraded with the latest equipment, and the streets were brightly lit.

What will streetlights be like in the future? According to scientists' predictions—as seen in the book "The World Fifty Years Hence"—the current arrangement of streetlights scattered here and there is too troublesome. It will only be necessary to install a very large streetlight in the air at a suitable location, connect it to a powerful electricity source, and with a turn of the switch, it will be as bright as the sun. At that time, perhaps even household lights will no longer be needed. However, when this kind of streetlight will be invented, please young people wait patiently! You will surely be able to see it.

Xiaoxitian 142

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 18: Qi Dang Gaozhong Flatteringly Rebukes the Clerk, Madam Acts Fiercely and Noisily Annoying.

He heard that Commissioner Lan upstairs was calling the tea boy downstairs, which meant that his colleagues upstairs had not handled things well. That was why he had to send another raw hand up there. Maybe if he took out twenty or thirty dollars to buy things, he could take advantage of Jia. So he answered with an "Oh" and ran upstairs. When he got to the Commissioner's door, he paused for a moment to catch his breath, and then went in unhurriedly. He saw Commissioner Jian leaning back in his chair with a pipe in his mouth, looking quite relaxed. There was a wine bottle on the table, and several empty cans. The air was thick with the smell of alcohol, probably after he had had his evening drink. His wife stood firmly with one hand on the table, glared at him and asked, "Are you the tea boy downstairs?" Ma San said, "Yes, Madam, what are your orders?" Mrs. Lan said, "What kind of woman lives downstairs? It's so late, and she's still crying?" Ma San didn't expect to be called up to answer such a question, and was a little unhappy. He replied, "She is the family member of a guest, I don't know why she's crying." Mrs. Lan said, "Are you tea boys only good for eating? It's so late, and the guest is still crying. Of course there's a reason, why don't you ask?" Ma San said with a faint smile, "How can I, as a tea boy, go and ask a female guest why she is crying?" Mrs. Lan slapped the table and said, "This guy is outrageous. I say one thing, and he contradicts me with another." Ma San thought to himself, "I'm a tea boy downstairs, I don't serve you." So he replied, "I'm a tea boy downstairs, I don't care about the guests upstairs." As he said this, he turned around and walked out. Mrs. Lan slapped the table repeatedly and said, "Come back! Come back! Who are you talking to? If you say another word, I'll break your legs!" (310)

Royal Incense Piao Miao Lu 143

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

This is really time-consuming, and it requires patience; also, usually, when she wants to wash her hands, we must be there to serve her, and after washing, we must use a towel to pat them dry in the same way. Even the floral lotion she applies to her face every night is also applied to her hands. This task is performed by the lady-in-waiting who is on duty that night.

In addition to this, there are countless ways that the Empress Dowager wants to beautify herself!

One of them is to take ground pearl powder once every ten days. I have never carefully calculated how many pearls she needs for each serving of pearl powder. I only know that the pearls used for grinding the powder are all small pearls, generally round and lustrous, and very valuable. Each time the powder is ground, it is about a small teaspoon. The teaspoon is made of silver, and the style is different from ordinary ones. It is probably specially made for the Empress Dowager to take pearl powder. This practice of taking pearl powder has been going on for decades and has never been interrupted. It has almost become a fixed system; every ten days, almost at the same time, the eunuch in charge of grinding the pearl powder uses a piece of yellow silk to hold the silver spoon and presents the ground pearl powder to the Empress Dowager.

The Empress Dowager doesn't need to ask any more questions. As soon as she sees this person coming in, she knows it's time to take the pearl powder. (410)

Biographical Sketches

The Queen of Sark, England 144

— Haike

There is a small island, a country in its own right under the flag of the British Empire, which is probably the strangest country in the world. Ruling this country is a lady, and although her country is small, it even has a parliament, but it only meets three times a year. The lady herself is the chairman, and she enjoys various privileges inherited from ancient times.

This island country is called Sark and is located in the English Channel. This queen does not have the title of "Queen," but is only called "Dame of Sark." Sark Island's neighbor, a small island called Brecqhou, is being put up for sale. If someone buys this island, they can obtain the qualification of a member of parliament, because not only can they be the owner of this island, but they can also occupy a seat in the ancient parliament of Sark. Brecqhou Island is only three-quarters of a mile long and half a mile wide, with a total of three islanders, two houses, one field, a curved road one mile long, a pier for steamboats, and various fishing interests. Whoever buys this island must pay one pound sterling to "Dame of Sark" for every thirteen pounds of the purchase price, because Brecqhou is under the jurisdiction of Sark Island, and this money is a special tax.

"Dame of Sark" is the only female leader in the British Empire and enjoys full administrative power. In addition to serving as the chairman of the parliament, she can also raise pigeons, open mills, or keep a female dog, which are her exclusive rights and cannot be enjoyed by anyone else on the island. All land on the island that is sold must have her consent, and a special tax of one pound sterling is levied on every thirteen pounds of the purchase price.

Sark Island has a total of forty fields. The owners of the fields must pay various taxes of different qualities. The strangest thing is that there is a tax that requires each household to pay poultry to "Dame of Sark" according to the number of windows in the house. Every window is required to pay one poultry, and so on. In order to save money, the islanders have to open fewer windows on their houses.

The current "Dame of Sark" is Mrs. D. Beaumont, the widow of a British cavalry officer. Her great-grandfather, T. G. Collings, bought the island in 1852. After his death, the property was inherited by his daughter-in-law, and then passed on to Mrs. Beaumont. Because she likes to travel and has traveled all over the world, she has seen a lot and has a broad perspective. Ruling this small island of Sark is not a big deal. Mrs. Beaumont has six children, and it is unknown which one will inherit her and become the owner of Sark Island.

Sark Island is very small, but its responsibilities are not light. Relying on her talents, she has taken on the task. For example, hygiene planning, school examinations, road repairs, harbor construction, fishery legislation, and tax formulation are all the responsibilities of the island government and are all handled by her personally. Everything is well organized. The island's parliament meets only three times a year, and she chairs all meetings to discuss all matters of reform and innovation on the island. The parliament also serves as the supreme court, and if there are any disputes among the people, they must ultimately be appealed to the parliament.

Sark Island has the right to participate in any ceremonies held in the British Empire. Mrs. Beaumont attends as "Dame of Sark" and represents the island. She is the only busy person on the island, handling both internal and external affairs.

Sark Island pays tribute to King George of England, and the title is very special, because it adheres to the ancient system, so it still uses the old title of Duke of Normandy. All documents presented to the King of England are in French, calling him "My King, My Duke," "Re Roi, Nofre Duc." This is also a very special matter. The people of Sark Island never speak English; they speak the purest Norman French, which is said to still preserve the language of William the Conqueror and his followers.

Sports News

Mayor Wu Personally Cuts Ribbon at Grand Opening of City Swimming Pool Yesterday 145

Ms. Chen Baoxuan Performs Water Entry Ceremony; Male and Female Athletes Hold Exhibition Matches; Officially Open to the Public Starting Today

The Shanghai City Swimming Pool held its opening ceremony yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. Mayor Wu personally cut the ribbon and delivered the opening speech. Ms. Chen Baoxuan performed the water entry ceremony, and athletes from the city preparing to participate in the National Games participated in exhibition matches. More than two thousand people from all walks of life traveled from afar to visit and unanimously praised the construction of the swimming pool. The pool is officially open to the public starting today, with tickets still priced at twenty cents. A detailed account of yesterday's events follows:

Attendees

Mayor Wu, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan Chu Minyi, Madam Jiang (Chen Bijun), Secretary-General of the Municipal Government Yu Hongjun, Secretaries Tang Shixuan and Chang Tingrong, Section Chief Li Dachao, Director of Education Pan Gongzhan, Director of Public Utilities Xu Peihuang, Director of Health Li Ting'an, Director of the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau Jian Shiqin, as well as Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Xiaopei, Yan Fuqing, Rong Zongjing, Hu Xiyuan, Lu Bohong, Dong Dayou, Shen Siliang, Jiang Jianbai, and over two thousand spectators from all walks of life. Li Dachao of the Municipal Government served as the chief host, with Lin Yannan, Wang Keyong, Lü Hailan, and Zhang Yinhuai serving as hosts.

Enthusiastic Scene

Before 1:00 PM yesterday afternoon, vehicles on Jiangwan Road were bumper to bumper, and pedestrians were shoulder to shoulder, all heading to the city center to attend the ceremony. The China General Omnibus Company specially operated one-way buses directly to the pool, which were packed with passengers, leaving no room. Spectators along the way simply could not board. In front of the swimming pool, there was a constant flow of traffic and a sea of people, truly an unprecedented sight.

A Glimpse of the Décor

The opening ceremony platform was set up on the third floor of the swimming pool, with guests below and spectators in the left and right stands. In front of the platform, Party and national flags were crossed, with a portrait of Sun Yat-sen hanging in the center. Small Party and national flags were hung all around the stands of the pool, fluttering in the wind, bright and eye-catching. The fourth floor of the pool was surrounded by red ribbons, which shone in contrast with the green water. All equipment was neat and clean, leaving the audience in awe. A temporary wireless broadcast system was installed in front of the platform, and speeches and reports could be heard clearly throughout the pool.

Mayor's Speech

The ceremony began at 2:00 PM, with Lin Yannan as the master of ceremonies. After the Public Security Bureau band played music and the ceremony proceeded as planned, Mayor Wu delivered the opening speech, saying: "Distinguished guests, today is the opening ceremony of the Shanghai City Swimming Pool. I am deeply grateful for the presence of guests from all walks of life and extend a warm welcome. The swimming pool is one of the most important buildings in Shanghai's municipal sports venues. Construction began in November of last year and was completed in August of this year. The swimming pool is 50 meters long and 20 meters wide, with a maximum depth of 11 feet and a minimum depth of 4 feet. The stands can accommodate over 4,000 spectators. The pool water is equipped with a filtration system that changes and disinfects the water every six hours. After the swimming pool opens today, exhibition matches will be held. Starting tomorrow, it will be open daily from 2:00 PM to 6:00 PM. I hope that the citizens of Shanghai can make full use of this swimming pool, as swimming is one of the main subjects in sports. There is an old Chinese saying that southerners are good at swimming, and northerners are good at riding. This may have been the case in the past due to the development of living habits, but today, both southerners and northerners should swim. I hope that the citizens of Shanghai will make full use of the swimming pool and that their swimming skills will improve day by day. Shanghai is a very large city with over 3 million citizens, and one public swimming pool is not enough. I hope that public swimming pools can be built step by step in different districts within the possible scope of public financial resources to meet the needs of the citizens. Thank you very much for attending today's ceremony."

Ribbon Cutting and Water Entry

After the Mayor finished his speech, he personally went down the steps to perform the ribbon-cutting ceremony. The guests applauded. Then Ms. Chen Baoxuan performed the water entry ceremony, diving into the water from the high diving board and swimming 50 meters freestyle. Immediately afterwards, team leader Peng Sanmei led over 30 male and female athletes in formation around the pool. The men wore black swimsuits, and the women wore yellow swimming caps and blue "Three Wheels" brand swimsuits. They circled half a lap around the pool, to the applause of the audience.

Exhibition Matches

Immediately following was the exhibition match. Of the original thirteen events scheduled, the blind swimming event did not take place. The results of each event were satisfactory. The 50-meter freestyle performance by six-year-old Yang Qiying attracted much attention from the audience, with a time of one minute, thirty-six and eight-tenths seconds. After the performance ended around 5:00 PM, guests from all walks of life were free to enter the pool, and everyone dispersed around 6:00 PM. Coach Peng Sanmei issued the starting commands for the exhibition match. In the first event, the men's 50-meter freestyle, Liang Yisheng won first place by a centimeter, followed by Huang Yuexiong and Zhang Rongguang, who were only about two inches apart. This is a new city record. Next was the women's 50-meter freestyle. Liu Wenxian led the way, while Jiang Aixian and Yang Chuanying tried their best to catch up. Ms. Liu reached the finish line with a lead of one and a half meters. In the women's 200-meter breaststroke, Jian Erjie had already surpassed the first person by more than two meters at 30 meters after entering the water. She finished with an excellent time of three minutes and seventeen and four-tenths seconds, setting a new Shanghai record. Next was the women's 50-meter breaststroke. Ms. He Wenjin, one of the three heroines newly arrived in Shanghai from Qingdao, also participated in the competition. Zhou Xiuling led by half a meter, Zhang Jiazhen was half a meter behind He, and Wu Juanjuan trailed. The 400-meter freestyle was one of the most exciting scenes yesterday. Shi Bogen led the way after the start, and reached the finish line 80 meters ahead of the second person, with a time of six minutes and eight seconds. The participants in the women's 50-meter backstroke were the Yang sisters and He Wenjing and Li Lingli from Qingdao. Yang Zhongying and He Wenjing competed fiercely, with Yang leading by half an arm. Jian Erming in the men's 100-meter backstroke went out of bounds, allowing Xu Shouqiang to lead by one arm to the finish line. Liang Weisheng and Huang Yuexiong fought fiercely in the men's 100-meter freestyle. In the last five meters, Liang leaped to the finish line, pushing Huang back about a foot, with a time of one minute and eight and eight-tenths seconds. Next, six-year-old Yang Qiying performed the 50-meter, with excellent form. Liu Suxian won the women's 100-meter freestyle again. The last was the 150-meter medley relay, with four groups participating. The strengths were balanced. The first group had a time of one minute and twenty-five and five-tenths seconds. The diving and artistic performances were not formal performances due to the lack of sturdiness of the diving boards. The performance ended at half past four, and everyone dispersed happily.

This City Participates in National Games Football Trial Match Yesterday: Blue Team Wins Over White Team 6-3 146

To Whom Will the Football Championship Belong? In the current 6th National Games, it is indeed an important question worthy of exploration. According to reports collected from all parties, cities such as Guangzhou, Hong Kong, Beiping, overseas Chinese, and Shanghai all have the same enthusiastic ambition to win the championship. Shanghai, by virtue of its home advantage, cannot be underestimated. Therefore, the Shanghai Municipal Football Team's first trial match yesterday was held under this mission at Zhongyuan.

Blue vs. White

Trial matches are different from ordinary matches; the purpose is to observe the individual skills of the players and the overall cooperation. The outcome is not important. Often, one team focuses on attacking, while the other team focuses on defending. For example, yesterday, the blue team focused on attacking, while the white team focused on defending. The blue team's five forwards were Wan Xianghua, Xu Wenshou, Dai Linjing, Chen Jiaqiu, and Jia Youliang. Li Yichen and Mu Xing were deliberately held back, presumably to be used in the future. The five forwards performed well individually, but their cooperation was not yet perfect. However, it was not easy to see them perform like this for the first time. Looking to the future, there is reason to be optimistic. The white team focused on defense. The goalkeeper was originally scheduled to be Xu Heng, but his name was omitted from the list, so he did not attend, and Zhang Rongcai replaced him. The inner defenders Li Ning and Jiang Shanjing, the central defenders Xu Jingcheng, Shang Xiang, and Liang Shutang were in the first half. There were slight changes in the second half. Comparing the two, the former was more impressive. The white team once suffered a penalty outside the penalty area line. Li and Jiang stood side by side in front of the ball to form a human wall. The two forwards stood to the left and right of the goal, forming a triangle. The defender stood in the center of the goal, directly leaving the opponent with no way to shoot. This kind of arrangement had not been seen in Shanghai before and is worth mentioning.

Trial Match Recap

The game started at 3:30 PM. After a long period of mixed play, Feng Yunyou, the central defender of the blue team, intercepted a ball halfway, picked it up, and sent it forward. Xu Wenkui met it head-on and shot back into the net. Following this, Dai Linjing took advantage of the fact that the entire white team was out, and the inner city was empty, and gently dialed it in again, making it 2-0. Before long, with the assistance of Chen Jiaqiu, Dai scored another goal. This was the most prosperous era for the blue team (attacking team). The white team reorganized its formation and stepped up its defense. The forwards also launched attacks several times, and finally Liu Zuxiu won back a goal. The first half ended 3-1. In the second half, the line-up changed dramatically. Zhong Yuxiang first scored a goal for the white team. Unexpectedly, Liang Shutang sowed the seeds of disaster and was penalized with a penalty kick. Chen Jiaqiu of the blue team did not miss, and the score became 4-2. In the last ten minutes, Xu Wenkui and Chen Jiaqiu of the blue team each scored a goal, and Liu Zuru of the white team also scored a goal. As a result, the blue team won 6-3.

Ministry of Education Orders Sichuan Education Department to Handle Matters Concerning Provincial Agricultural College and Other Schools 161

According to an inspection report, the Ministry of Education recently issued an order to the Sichuan Provincial Education Department, stating roughly that: The Ministry had previously sent personnel to inspect the Sichuan Provincial Agricultural College, the Provincial Industrial College, the Sichuan Rural Construction College, and the Provincial Ceramics Vocational School. Based on the reports received and after detailed review, the actual conditions of operation of these colleges and schools do not match their reputations. Separate handling measures should be determined. Apart from previously "briefly informing by telegram" regarding the Agricultural and Industrial Colleges, further instructions are now given as follows:

1. Sichuan Provincial Agricultural College

Upon investigation, the college currently has two departments, Agronomy and Forestry, with just over forty students. It has an affiliated high school with three classes. The regular funding is only over forty-six thousand yuan, which has not always been fully disbursed and is insufficient to cover salaries and expenses. Most of the teachers hold concurrent positions. The teaching materials rely solely on lectures, with no opportunities for practical training. The school buildings are dilapidated, and the equipment is extremely lacking. The practice fields are not utilized. The current state of the college is largely unsatisfactory. Starting from this year, it should be immediately merged into the National Sichuan University, combining the two departments into an Agronomy and Forestry Department. The university should rigorously reorganize the department, enrich the faculty and equipment to facilitate teaching. The original funding should be allocated to Sichuan University for its disposal. The school property and practical equipment should be received by the Provincial Department first, and then transferred to Sichuan University for management. The affiliated high school should be managed by the Provincial Department in a coordinated manner.

2. Sichuan Provincial Industrial College

Upon investigation, the college currently has three departments: Mechanical Engineering, Applied Chemistry, and Mining and Metallurgy, with seventy-three students. It has an affiliated high school with three classes. The regular funding is only sixty-two thousand yuan, which has often been largely reduced, with the largest portion used for new salaries and office expenses. The president and most of the teachers hold concurrent positions and are often absent at will. The teaching materials focus heavily on lectures while neglecting experiments. The students' level is very low, and the equipment is outdated and simple, no longer applicable. The college's operating conditions are largely inappropriate. Starting from this year, the funding should be allocated to Chongqing University for its disposal. The remaining school property and various equipment should be taken over by the Provincial Department and used to establish an industrial vocational school. The affiliated high school should also be managed by the Provincial Department in a coordinated manner.

3. Sichuan Rural Construction College

Upon investigation, the organization of the college includes not only the college section but also a research and experimental department, an agricultural technology personnel training school, a rural education experimental zone, and an agricultural experiment field. The college's undergraduate program is divided into a Rural Society Department and an Agricultural Department, with only over fifty students. The entrance qualifications do not meet the standards. The students in the training school have a level equivalent to junior high school. The regular funding is allocated from the provincial education funds, totaling over one hundred thousand and two thousand yuan in the twenty-third fiscal year. The original purpose of establishing the college was to focus on rural construction work, which does not fall under the jurisdiction of educational administrative organs. Therefore, educational funds should not be used. Moreover, the use of the "College" designation is inconsistent with the organizational regulations of National Chung Hsing University. Starting from this year, it should change its name and purpose. Together with the agricultural experiment field, it should be transferred to the Construction Department or the Civil Affairs Department for management, with funding provided from the provincial treasury.

4. Provincial Ceramics Vocational School

Upon investigation, the school has an undergraduate program and a practical training class. The undergraduate program has forty-nine students, and the practical training class has nineteen students. The entrance qualification is junior high school graduation. The length of study is one year for the practical training class and three years for the undergraduate program. The regular funding received is over seventeen thousand yuan from the province. The students lack practical training, and the internal management is poor. The school's structure is essentially that of a senior vocational nature and should not continue to use the "Vocational School" designation. Starting from this year, it should be immediately renamed Senior Ceramics Vocational School. The current principal's mismanagement should be addressed immediately, and specialized talent should be appointed to thoroughly reorganize the school. The order is issued to the Department to comply with and implement the instructions accordingly.

Songjiang County Education Bureau Director Shen's Reply to Chen Deqi's Letter Regarding the Joint Establishment of a Normal School by Seven Counties 162

The newspaper recently reported on Chen Deqi's letter to the Songjiang County Education Bureau regarding the merger of the female normal schools of seven counties. Now, we have Director Shen's reply: "To My Respected Teacher Xipeng, I received your quick letter yesterday and respectfully learned of your concerns regarding the merger of the female normal schools of seven counties. This matter was decided at a meeting convened by the Education Department on August 21st, attended by the responsible personnel from the seven counties in the province. Before that, we had not received any other official documents to cease operations. The merged school is located in Huangdu Township, not Qixia Township. Your letter seems to contain a misunderstanding based on hearsay. Your letter states that local original funds should be used to operate local original undertakings. This is originally determined by the former Jiangsu Provincial Government, ‘using original funds in original places for original undertakings.’ I am also a son of one of the counties and will naturally follow the local elders and devote myself wholeheartedly. However, due to the Education Bureau's position, it is bound by the Department's decision to implement this case. However, I did not attend the provincial meeting due to illness. The meeting did not discuss the quota allocation for our county. At the concluding meeting convened by our bureau yesterday (the 7th) as ordered, I proposed that the original quotas of the seven counties should be maintained, that is, fourteen for Songjiang and seven for each of the other six counties. This has been passed and reported to the Department for record. I hope that it will be approved. This is something to comfort Teacher Chen Wu. Regarding your suggestion that it would be more convenient to merge with Songjiang County Normal School and your request for me to propose this, not only would the geographical relationship between the counties make it unlikely to be satisfactory, but the instructions had already been given, and there was no opportunity to propose it for discussion. I hope you understand. Other details are in the merger method and the minutes of the concluding meeting, which I enclose for your reference. I offer my respectful regards and wish you well. Respectfully yours, Shen Lianlu, September 4th."

Appendix (1) Merger Method: 1. In addition to the original funding of 4,000 yuan for Huangdu Township Normal School, the rest will be subsidized by provincial funds. 2. The students already enrolled in this session will be merged immediately. Thereafter, recruitment will be conducted once every four years, admitting both male and female students and raising the level of education. 3. Newly recruited public-funded students will be screened by Huangdu Township Normal School. Those not admitted will be allowed to study in county middle schools. 4. Private-funded students currently in the second year will be allowed to transfer to Songjiang County Normal School or the original first year of the seven-county township normal schools. Students currently in the first year will be sent to the provincial township normal schools of Wujiang, Huangdu, Louxia, or county middle schools. All will be admitted only if they pass the summer examination, and they will continue to pay tuition according to the original quota. (2) Minutes of the Concluding Meeting: Concluding meeting of the Joint Establishment of Female Normal Schools by Songjiang, Fengxian, Jinshan, Shanghai, Nanhui, Qingpu, and Chuansha Counties, September 2, 24th year. Attendees: Zhu Shijun, Jinshan; Shen Zhi, Shen Jixi, Chuansha; Gu Cuishi (representative); Wang Hongwen, Fengxian; Xu Jie (representative); Yuan Weiwen, Qingpu; Zhu Changlin, Shanghai; Chen Guobao, Nanhui; Zhang Jianqian (representative); Shen Lianbi, Songjiang; Liao (Director) of the Female Normal School. Chairman: Shen Lianbi. Recorder: Zhu Pi. Opening ceremony (omitted). Matters for Discussion: Item 1: The Department has stipulated a merger method, but only provides principles for the transfer of original first and second-year students. How should this be arranged to facilitate their enrollment as soon as possible? Decision: (1) The sixteen Songjiang students in the original second year will transfer to Songjiang County Normal School. The seven Qingpu students will transfer to the township normal schools of Kunshan, Qingpu, and Jiading. The three Jinshan students and four Shanghai students, three Fengxian students and three Nanhui students will transfer to the county normal schools in their respective locations. The one Wuxian and one Jiashan student(s) will also transfer to their respective county normal schools. The director of the Huangdu Township Normal School, Teng, stated that his school has fifteen vacancies in the third year and should immediately report for the right to transfer those students. (2) The original first-year students (now to be promoted to the second year) and the original second-year repeaters, totaling thirty-seven, will all transfer to Huangdu Township Normal School due to the inconvenient transportation to Wujiang Qixia. It should be immediately reported and requested that a second-year class be added at Huangdu Township Normal School to accommodate them. Otherwise, the Department should assign the students by name to the three township normal schools of Huangdu, Wujiang, and Qixia to avoid disputes. (3) The original first-year repeaters should be sent to Huangdu Township Normal School together with the public-funded students recruited in this session for screening. Those not admitted after screening, except for Chuansha County students who will transfer to Nanhui Girls' Middle School, will transfer to the county middle schools in their respective counties. The above points will be submitted to the Department for approval by the Songjiang County Education Bureau immediately. Item 2: Director Liao proposed, "Teacher contracts for this semester have already been issued. How should this be handled? Also, how should the 667.6 yuan already paid in August (with detailed accounts) and future payments be spent?" Decision: The issue of contracts will be reported to the Department for instructions. The funds to be spent in August and September should be allocated from the school's regular expenses for August, subject to approval by the Department, and the Songjiang County Education Bureau will report to the Department and implement the instructions. Item 3: Director Liao proposed, "The school's new buildings are under construction. What should be done in light of this change?" Decision: The entire construction funding was raised by Director Liao. Director Liao should handle it with due care. Item 4: How should the school buildings be kept safe and utilized? Decision: The Songjiang County Education Bureau will be responsible for the building's safe-keeping and utilization. If the seven counties need to use it for new undertakings in the future, it should be handed over for use. Item 5: The Department's merger method does not clearly specify the student quotas for the seven counties. Please discuss. Decision: Since the students of this grade are managed with the original funding of the seven counties merged into Huangdu Township Normal School as ordered by the Department, the student quotas should still follow the original method, with 14 for Songjiang and 7 for each of the other counties. These should be named as the "Public-Funded Students of the Former Song Dynasty's Seven Counties", and the Songjiang County Education Bureau should report it to the Department for record. Item 6: Director Liao proposed, "Various books and registers for student use were ordered from bookstores with the school's name printed on them and cannot be returned. How should this be handled?" Decision: The Songjiang County Education Bureau will send a letter to Huangdu Township Normal School to purchase and use them.
