Economic Special

Promoting and Controlling the Transportation Network Plan 165

— Wu Shaozeng

A nation's transportation should have a complete plan and system. It is by no means enough to build some railways and highways, and open up some waterways and airways. Its distribution and organization must be like the human body's circulatory system, accessible everywhere, and connected at every point, forming a kind of transportation network to demonstrate its maximum efficiency. Otherwise, if there are phenomena of fragmentation, or only the pursuit of local development, the direct impact on the transportation industry and the indirect impact on the national economy will certainly not be insignificant.

However, the so-called transportation network cannot be created solely by a single transportation agency. The elements of a transportation network are three:

(1) Tightness in time: For example, when traveling from Route A to Route B, upon arriving at the end of Route A, one can immediately board a vehicle on Route B; or, when arriving at the destination station by railway, there are immediately highway buses or waterway ships to接运(pick up and transport) passengers and goods. Passengers are spared the tedium of sitting and waiting, and goods avoid the regret of altered quality or delayed sales opportunities. This is the effect of timeliness.

(2) Adjustment in space: For example, where there are waterways, no railways are built parallel to the waterways; where there are railways, no highways are built parallel to the railways. Efforts are made to distribute various transportation facilities evenly, so that one area does not feel congested with passengers and goods, struggling to cope; while the other area feels that there are too few passengers and goods, wasting capital. This is the effect of spatial adjustment.

(3) Adjustment in economy: For example, for goods that are large in quantity and transported to distant places, trains or ocean liners are used for loading and transporting; for small quantities transported to nearby places, trucks or inland river ships are used for loading and transporting; for small quantities that need to be delivered quickly, airplanes are used for loading and transporting. The same goes for passengers: for long distances, they can take trains, ocean liners, or airplanes; for short distances, they can take cars or inland river ships. The freight rates for passengers and goods are based on what merchants and passengers can afford, so that the economy in terms of time and cost can be considered, and each can be accommodated. This is the effect of economic adjustment.

However, to reap the benefits of timeliness and adjustment in transportation, and to demonstrate the effectiveness of the transportation network, there are only two ways: one is the regulation of the transportation industry, and the other is the cooperation of various modes of transportation. The former relies on the government's overall planning, and the latter is the full connection of various modes of transportation themselves. The railway is the lifeline of transportation, and it should fulfill its part of the responsibility for the layout of the transportation network along the line. Therefore, in recent years, state-owned railways have been carrying out connecting transportation with various land, water, and air parties, step by step, sparing no effort, which is commendable.

However, past intermodal transport facilities cannot be said to have exhausted their capabilities, and there are still many areas to be improved and promoted in the future. The following are some of the major points:

(A) Improving Railway Intermodal Transport: Regarding the improvement of passenger intermodal transport, several points can be mentioned as follows:

(1) For passenger intermodal transport, the tightness of time is the most important. In the past, although the various railway lines have strived to connect train schedules through schedule network meetings, except for the direct crossing of the Yangtze River for the Shanghai-Beijing through train, which is not a problem, the connection of vehicles from other lines has not been completely tight. Further improvements should be made. Even if the plan for inter-railway passenger cars to cross tracks cannot be realized for a while, we should often plan to closely connect the schedules of intermodal transport with each other, so that passengers can obtain the greatest economy in terms of time.

(2) American railways also operate highways, on the one hand to seek the nourishment of the railway itself, and on the other hand to make it convenient for passengers to接运 (pick up and transport). If there is a need to build highways along the railway line in our country, and no other party can handle it for a while, then the railway may as well invest in it. Moreover, the highway operated by the railway itself radiates from the railway trunk line, which is especially beneficial for arranging the transportation network.

(3) Intermodal passengers mostly travel long distances. According to the current fare calculation, the longer the journey, the higher the cost. Therefore, unless they have huge assets or urgent matters, few are willing to take this route. In the future, in order to develop intermodal transport business, it is not advisable to give discounts on intermodal ticket prices or provide other conveniences to promote it.

(4) Intermodal passengers often need to stay in hotels after arriving at the connecting station or terminal station. If the place is a metropolis or commercial port, there is no problem; but if it is a remote town, it is very distressing to have no good accommodation. Therefore, the railway should pay attention to the hotel facilities at the intermodal connecting station or terminal station. If there is a lack of a suitable hotel in the area, the railway may as well run it itself. The scale does not have to be too large, but the facilities should be clean and tidy, so that passengers can feel at home.

(5) Railway passenger intermodal transport, in addition to the interconnection of domestic railway lines, must be further extended to foreign countries, in order to promote international tourism. Our country has famous mountains and scenic spots everywhere, which should be widely publicized, and intermodal sightseeing passenger cars should be set up to attract them, which will be of great benefit to the railway business and the national economy. Therefore, the intermodal transport between our country's railways and foreign railways or ships should also be actively prepared.

Regarding the convenience of freight intermodal transport, there are also several aspects that urgently need to be improved:

(1) To stipulate the travel time of freight cars. Although intermodal freight transport has been carried out on various lines, the travel dates have not been stipulated. It is often difficult for freight merchants to accurately estimate the arrival date of goods, so that the market price cannot be predicted. Therefore, the travel dates should be stipulated to increase the convenience of freight merchants, and it is also easy to调度 (dispatch) railway vehicles, so that they will not be wasted.

(2) To set special prices for intermodal transport of bulk goods. Because various lines have special price regulations for transporting bulk goods, only a few have special prices for intermodal transport goods. In the future, in order to seek practical cooperation in cloth transportation and sales, various lines should select the bulk goods produced and agree on special prices, so that supply and demand can be adjusted and prices can be balanced.

(3) To unify the calculation of freight. For example, the percentage of freight surcharges and the percentage of handling fees are different on each line, with some adding, some not adding, some adding 10%, and some adding 20%, which makes the freight calculation extremely complicated. Not only can freight merchants not check, but road staff also feel troubled by this. Therefore, it should be simplified to facilitate calculation and make it easy for freight merchants to understand.

(4) The loading and unloading fee should be collected together with the freight. The loading and unloading fees of various lines are determined according to the situation of their location. Although the amount is small, the system is extremely complicated. At present, as a temporary measure, the loading and unloading fees are temporarily collected by each line. For intermodal goods, the unloading fee paid by the sender is collected by the arrival station; and the loading fee paid by the recipient is collected by the departure station, but it cannot be filled in the freight bill, only a miscellaneous receipt is given. Therefore, all freight merchants must pay the loading and unloading fees for intermodal goods separately from the freight bill, which is not only troublesome, but also prone to overcharging. Therefore, the loading and unloading fee should be collected at the same time as the freight, so as to avoid separate payment by freight merchants, and to enable the consignee to pick up the goods only with the freight bill, without having to take into account the payment of loading and unloading fees, which will definitely increase a lot of convenience.

(B) Promoting Intermodal Transport by Water, Land, and Air: The purpose of railways and various land, water, and air parties in handling intermodal transport is nothing more than to form a flat and three-dimensional transportation network. The denser the organization and the wider the scope of this transportation network, the more it can demonstrate its great function. Therefore, in the future, all waterways and highways along the railway line, except those parallel to the railway, should be connected with it. We should also contact the air routes to organize intermodal transport; and in addition to passengers and luggage packages, we must also follow the examples of European and American countries and extend it to goods, so that the specialties of various places can expand the scope of transportation and sales, and achieve the purpose of corresponding supply and demand.

(C) Expanding the Service Scope of Business Offices: For the contact and transportation of luggage, parcels, and less-than-carload freight between inland areas and cities, the business office is actually its hub. Although several lines have now set up business offices, due to location relations, their service scope is still biased towards major cities, and has not been able to penetrate into inland towns. Therefore, in the future, all stations along the line should be uniformly implemented as business offices, that is, all service items of the business office should be handled concurrently by the staff of each station. In addition to selling passenger tickets, special attention should be paid to the往來運送(round-trip transportation) of luggage, parcels, and less-than-carload freight, and business office agencies should be set up everywhere in inland cities and towns to closely contact local shipping or汽軍(motorized military force, assumed typo) companies. All luggage, parcels, and less-than-carload freight transported in and out of the inland areas will be handled at a low cost, and all procedures for starting tickets, picking up goods, and划付欵項 (remitting funds) will be handled on their behalf. In this way, inland areas and cities will be營打成一片 (united into one), which will undoubtedly help to prosper the rural economy.

Moreover, examining a country's transportation, it is nothing more than four types: railway, waterway, highway, and airway. However, these four have their own natural strengths, and cannot be regarded as the same. Trains and ocean liners are suitable for long-distance travel and transportation of large quantities of perishable goods because of their high cost. Inland river boats and road vehicles are suitable for short-distance travel and transportation of small quantities of goods because of their lower cost. Airplanes are especially suitable for long-distance urgent travel and巡輸 (patrolling and transporting) of mail or valuables because of their particularly high speed. In addition to ordinary passenger and freight transportation, which contains economic relations, each also bears a national defense mission. Then, from the standpoint of the entire country, for these four types of transportation undertakings, we should seek to individually develop their natural strengths, so that they can help promote the prosperity of the national economy in peacetime, and can also express their national defense effectiveness in the event of an emergency. To achieve this, I believe that there are five points that should be paid close attention to:

(1) For various transportation undertakings, it is advisable to manage them in a unified way, so that the運價 (freight rates) of each and their mutual contact are regulated in order to achieve the effect of adjustment and avoid the drawback of being偏枯 (one-sided). Even if not, the administrative links in charge of transportation should also cooperate closely to協謀 (jointly plan) the balanced development of each transportation mode.

(2) For various transportation undertakings, it is advisable to treat them equally, not to助此以敵彼 (help this to defeat that), nor to益彼而損此 (benefit that and damage this); otherwise, the competition between them will inevitably become acute, resulting in a lose-lose situation. For example, in recent years, the United States has been专事援助 (specializing in assisting) waterways and highways, which has led to the衰疲 (decline) of railways. This is a cautionary tale.

(3) For the construction of railways, it is advisable to only build trunk lines, not branch lines, so as to concentrate elbow strength, fully extend the length of the railway, and connect important areas; and to将支綫之地位 (replace the position of branch lines), build highways to任 (take on) short-distance transportation. In this way, things will be twice as effective with half the effort, which is exactly in line with economic principles. The US railways did not have an overall plan beforehand, so there are now many conflicts between highways and railway branch lines, which are detrimental to both. Our country should not repeat the same mistake.

(4) For the construction of highways, it is advisable to have them纵横交错 (crisscross) with Qian (likely typo for rail) lines to form a transportation network, avoiding parallelism, or at least keeping a considerable distance apart; otherwise, if their起訖相同 (starting and ending points are the same) and the distance between them is very close, it will not only cause unfavorable competition between the two sides, but also, in terms of their individual effectiveness, I am afraid that they will not be able to充分表 (fully express) themselves.

(5) Regarding primitive transportation tools, it is advisable not to存姑息 (tolerate them), so as not to hinder the development of emerging transportation industries. Nowadays, world transportation is moving towards speed, distance, and safety. Our country should迎 (welcome)赶上 (catch up), eliminate the old and seek the new. When the new transportation industry is fully developed, the entire national economy will rely on it to prosper; otherwise,因噎廢食 (refraining from eating for fear of choking), the遗患 (hidden danger) will certainly not be insignificant.

In short, the various transportation industries in the country should相五联络 (mutually connect), and should never 相互妨 (hinder each other); should相互策應 (coordinate with each other), and should never相互背馳 (run counter to each other). Only by相互联络 (mutually connecting) and 策應(coordinating), can we mutually nourish, and exist in shared prosperity. Whether our country's transportation industry can obtain the greatest development and display the greatest effectiveness depends on this!

Furthermore, the ultimate goal of the transportation network is to enable the public to obtain transportation services with the lowest cost and the highest efficiency. However, in order to achieve this goal, in addition to close cooperation among various transportation industries, the government authorities must also find ways to promote economic equality and enable them to develop their natural strengths evenly. What are the ways? For various transportation industries, if their position is important, whether directly or indirectly, they must be given appropriate assistance to enable them to progress together. That's one. The taxes (or burdens) of various transportation industries should be based on the amount of their capital and the situation of their business, and fair tax rates should be核定 (verified and determined). That's two. The運費 (freight rates) of various types of transportation are related to the burden of the public, and should be详细爲釐核 (carefully checked) according to the weight of their cost, so as to ensure that they are fair. That's three. For various types of transportation, we should stipulate business standards, such as the equipment should be complete and precise, the procedures should be simple and fast, and the treatment of passengers should be respectful and courteous, all of which must meet the standards, so as to ensure that the public obtains the greatest comfort and convenience. That's four. All of these are of great importance to the development and efficiency of connecting transportation, and must not be neglected.

The Causes and Consequences of the Four Industry Disturbances in Wuxi 166

— Li Yinbei

At the end of August, the four industries of vegetables, rice beans, oil mills, and fresh meat in Wuxi, due to fertilizer problems and tax issues, successively experienced shutdowns and petitioning disturbances. This caused a serious panic in the entire Wuxi's food supply. The following is a narrative of the factual process and the discussion of the contents.

1. A Summary of the Facts

(1) Vegetable Farming Disturbance: Recently, Zhou Zude, Xu Renyi, Huang Xiamin, and more than a dozen others, raised 10,000 yuan to organize Xieji Agricultural Co., Ltd.; under the business department, they also jointly organized Xieji Office with Longshun, Yuanda, Rongfa, Shengsheng, Fuchang, Jinsheng, Daming, Yiji, Baoxing, 等昌(etc Chang), Deji, Huinong, Zengnong, Rongxing, Zhifa, Ruirui, Xinghua, Linong, Liangyi, Yuantun, Haoji, Shengtai, Jinji, Delying, Huafa and other twenty-five fertilizer firms. The entire county's vegetable farming industry believed that the office monopolized fertilizers,操從居奇 (manipulated prices), and harmed agriculture. Therefore, on the afternoon of August 28, more than a thousand vegetable farmers from all districts gathered and marched to the county party headquarters and the county government separately to petition. They demanded that the licenses be revoked and that the office be ordered to disband. More than 300 vegetable farmers also went to the Xieji office to demonstrate, resulting in a conflict. On the morning of the 29th, farmers from vegetable gardens everywhere sent people to guard the entrances of the five city gates, prohibiting the sale of vegetables into the city and stopping transactions. On the 30th, the vegetable farms outside the city also unanimously stopped trading. By this point, all vegetable farmers in the city had stopped operating.

(2) Rice Bean Industry Disturbance: The local rice bean industry previously received an order from the Jiangsu Department of Finance to collect temporary business tax on wheat on behalf of customers. The industry believed that the flour mills collected wheat and had already levied unified tax, and that the sale of wheat by the industry was of a brokerage nature: collecting business tax on behalf of customers was actually difficult to implement. At the beginning of last month, they convened all members of the industry to discuss countermeasures; it was decided to write to the county chamber of commerce, appealing to the Ministry of Finance to quickly order the Jiangsu Department of Finance to withdraw the order to collect temporary business tax on wheat. The Ministry of Finance, according to the report, believed that the collection of business tax by brokers was a collection from the seller; and had nothing to do with the unified tax. The objection was rejected! The industry applied repeatedly; and the dispute remained unresolved. Therefore, on August 29, more than 130 grain firms in the industry! More than 500 representatives went to the county government to petition. It was heard that if there were no results, they would also deal with it by stopping business.

(3) Oil Mill Industry Disturbance: The Guangdong Provincial Government imposed a national additional tax on imported oil cakes to fund the construction of Sun Yat-sen University. It was set to collect 25 cents per burden, starting on September 1. This caused strong opposition from the oil cake and杂粮(miscellaneous grains) industry in Shanghai, Hankou, Wuxi, Changzhou, Kunshan and other places in the country. In addition to sending representatives to a meeting in Shanghai to organize a petition group to petition the central and southwestern governments and argue reasonably; at the same time, the national oil mill industry unanimously suspended work on August 31. Hengde and Runfeng, two oil mills in Wuxi, had already suspended work on August 31.

(4) Fresh Meat Industry Disturbance: The Wuxi slaughter tax collection office, because from September 1 last year to the end of August this year, was contracted by Lu Zongyi and other five executive committee members of the meat industry association; there were several twists and turns due to the tax amount problem. Later, the towel county chamber of commerce仲裁(arbitrated) the matter and provided a letter of proof; and a final decision was announced. However, there were occasional delays in the payment of the money; resulting in huge arrears of tax money; the tax money in various townships was greatly affected. After several negotiations, the collection office reported to the county government; and the county magistrate限期(set a deadline) for the tax money to be paid. The collection office believed that if the tax money was not rectified, the future would be unimaginable; so it was decided to implement point-by-point collection starting on September 1. The point-by-point collection method was announced. On the fresh meat industry side, it was believed that the owed tax had been限繳 (deadline to pay) by the county magistrate. There was no need to change the collection method. In order to express their opposition, the entire county's fresh meat industry unanimously suspended business starting on September 1.

The economic pathology of the above four industry disturbances, we analyze it below.

2. Vegetable Farming Disturbance

First, let's discuss vegetable farming. The remote cause of the vegetable farming shutdown was a political issue of sanitation. We can understand this by reading the original text of the Wuxi Autonomous First District Chief's reply to the vegetable farming industry.

"...(1) The government's crackdown on pit latrines aims to address the unlimited number of pit latrines in streets and alleys. This is not in line with public health; and also has an impact on the municipal appearance. Therefore, we are cracking down on the excess ones, and preserving the appropriate amount of toilets. It is not that we are filling up all pit latrines..."

The pit latrines in Wuxi are truly everywhere; there is no street without a pit; no alley without a toilet. The people have never known that it is harmful to sanitation; and the government has never known that it is detrimental to the appearance. It's just that customs are deeply ingrained and there is no way to improve! However, the power of administration increases and decreases with history. The party-化政治(party-based politics) in Wuxi has lasted longer than any warlord politics. The crackdown on pit latrines has also been more than once. Because the result of the crackdown is always书虎不成 (drawing a tiger but failing to make it resemble one). The biggest problem is that there are no proper arrangements for excrement. This time, the clever government did not announce the proper disposal method beforehand, but the arrangements made by the government beforehand can be understood from the petition submitted by the farmers to the district office after the matter expanded.

"...Our rural villagers have always used fertilizer; they buy it from the mountains and use it in their villages. It is heard that some entrust brokers to buy it on their behalf: This has continued to this day, and there has been no harm. Recently, there is a Xieji Office, which at the same time关向 (sent to) the county government to obtain twenty-five licenses from Rongfa and other brokers. On the one hand, it cracks down on private pit latrines; on the other hand, it publicly announces in newspapers..."

The organization of fertilizer firms originally required first obtaining a license from the local competent authorities; and then it could operate. According to the investigation of the local newspaper, there were originally thirteen licenses for fertilizer firms in Wuxi; later, the firms gradually closed down: up to now, only eight licenses remain. This time, because of the organization of the Xieji Office, they simultaneously suddenly向(sent to) the county government to obtain eighteen new licenses. Together with the old licenses, there are a total of twenty-six licenses. From the viewpoint of the factual observation of "simultaneously suddenly obtaining licenses"; it is not difficult to depict the government's 사전(prior) arrangement. Then, the Xieji Office is just a 焦(likely typo for 點, dot) that caused the recent cause of the disturbance.

3. Rice Bean Industry Disturbance

Next, let's discuss the rice bean industry. The petitioning disturbance of the Wuxi rice bean industry this time was purely a political issue of taxation. The main cause of this problem can be said to be entirely a reflection of the economic pathology of the rice bean industry itself. Before this problem is solved, let's first discuss whether wheat business tax should be levied on brokers. In the past, the Jiangsu Provincial Government's opinion on the collection of business tax was that for wheat flour that had already been levied an ex-factory tax, if the flour mill set up offices in the interior to collect wheat; the provincial government considered it a trading act. In fact, the flour mill sends people to collect wheat, not for sale; but to make wheat flour. The two procedures are only two sections of one business. Buying wheat is the first part, and manufacturing flour and shipping it out of the factory is the latter part. Since the central government has already levied one, the local government must not re-levy the other. Later, the Ministry of Finance stipulated a method of exemption, and this kind of dispute was resolved. However, the sale of wheat by grain firms cannot be regarded as the same example; because they buy on one hand and sell on the other hand. Even if they buy on behalf of the flour mill, they will inevitably extract commissions. This kind of behavior is obviously two trading acts. The two sections of the one business activity of the flour mill sending personnel to collect wheat; are of course not the same. Then; why did the Wuxi rice bean industry know that it was two trading acts and still cause a petitioning disturbance? His predicament is not difficult to understand. Because the rice bean industry itself審 (examines) the internal cause of its own economic pathology; at this time and in this place, it is absolutely impossible to bear this legal tax. Assuming that the rice bean industry did not have an internal economic pathology; perhaps this petitioning disturbance would not have happened at all. Looking at Wuxi's rice market this year, it is the most depressed market since there has been a rice market. Foreign rice is accumulating; and rice prices are falling. It is predicted that by the end of this year, the entire county's rice industry will definitely shrink as a whole. This internal reason is hoping for government support. But unexpectedly,漏 (typo, should be 又) it was also hit by heavy rain, making this legal tax; become a苛政 (oppressive government) that disturbs the people and troubles businesses at this time and in this place.

4. Oil Mill Industry Disturbance

The shutdown of the Wuxi oil mill this time was entirely激動 (triggered) by the cause of畸形(abnormal) politics. This disturbance has spread across the country, and the farmers in Wuxi are also paying very close attention; because oil cake is the raw material for壅田(mounding fields) and feeding pigs. It is closely related to agricultural production. From the telegrams sent by industry associations in various places, it can be seen that the reason why this tax should not be levied has been discovered. But on the government side, it seems that they still don't know; even if they know, it seems that they only know that it is, but not why! It is clear that only imported fertilizer should be taxed, how can domestic goods also be forcibly pulled in together. Therefore; the economic pathology of the oil mill industry disturbance is a reflection of political disunity.

5. Fresh Meat Industry Disturbance

Finally, let's discuss the shutdown of the fresh meat industry. It is even more so to explain the internal causes of agricultural bankruptcy and falling prices. The market price of fresh meat in Wuxi is seven catties per yuan. Farmers think that raising pigs is unprofitable, and they are bringing all their piglets to the city; to sell them as soon as possible. Therefore, the supply of fresh meat exceeds demand; and the market price is increasingly weak. The fresh meat誧 (likely typo, shops) in order to get rid of current goods, are trying their best to sell meat貨(goods) on credit. This has led to a shortage of cash; poor turnover, and the outstanding slaughter tax money cannot be paid. In order to maintain their tax revenue, the slaughter tax collection office has no choice but to use the method of point-by-point taxation for relief. But on the fresh meat industry side, there are bound to be two difficulties that are difficult to resolve.

(1) Point-by-point taxation will inevitably require daily payment; and there is no room for overdue concessions. But in this depressed fresh meat industry, they may not be able to afford it financially.

(2) The previously slightly owed slaughter tax will cause difficulties in清償(clearing) it.

With these two layers of national difficulty; there is an expression of opposition to the shutdown.

6. Conclusion

The occurrence of the above four industry disturbances; were all激盪 (triggered) by political reasons. The damage of these disturbances to the national economy is extremely great. If we had reliable statistics, the losses this time would definitely be very alarming. Now our hope is;

(1) On the side of various industries, fortunately, do not use this uneconomical means of shutdown again as a tool to maintain your own economic organization.

(2) When good politics are implemented, I hope that various industries will be willing to accept some small委曲(grievances); and do not deal with them by uneconomical means. Otherwise, we must also try our best to avoid expressing ourselves by harming our own economic organizations.

(3) I hope that the government authorities. When implementing policies, must take this time and place as the premise. Never cause the public to have uneconomical misunderstandings.

Tung Oil: One of the Most Glorious Pages in History 181

Hankou Tung Oil Soars to 60 Yuan 182

Sufficient quantity of white tung oil is being sold less and less, while various foreign firms in Hankou are still trying their best to search for it. However, prices are rising higher and higher. At the end of the previous week, it was still selling for 52 yuan and 5 dimes per picul, but entering this past week, it was like a kite with a broken string, soaring straight into the sky, from 53 yuan to 54 yuan, to 55 yuan, to 57 yuan, to 58 yuan, and finally, as of Saturday, it had been sold to 60 yuan. The soaring price is unstoppable, and the market atmosphere believes that 70 yuan is just around the corner. Although various foreign firms are trying to adapt, they are also buying insufficient quantities. However, when sufficient quantities are available, they are still competing for them, resulting in an unprecedented surge, creating an unprecedented situation in the market, which is truly one of the most glorious pages in the history of tung oil.

"Shen Bao" Medicine Weekly

On Typhoid Fever, Part Five (Under the Sun) 183

— Yu Yunxiu

The pulse's movement entirely depends on the heart's movement. The heart's movement consists of a contraction and an expansion. During contraction, the blood stored in the heart chambers is forced out and enters the vessels, causing them to expand. Simultaneously, the blood within the vessels moves forward. This is the true principle of the pulse's movement. When the heart doesn't move, neither does the pulse; the number of movements of the heart equates to the number of movements of the pulse. This is true not only for the radial artery at the cun, guan, and chi positions of both hands, but for all arteries throughout the body. All arteries that can be felt by hand, such as the anterior auricular artery, the dorsalis pedis artery, and the carotid artery, can be pressed to verify this empirically. However, when the heart is extremely weak, each contraction expels only a small amount of blood, insufficient to cause a noticeable expansion of the blood vessels, thus no pulse can be felt. Therefore, there are instances of the heart moving but the pulse not moving (modern medicine calls this pulseless contraction). There has never been a case of the pulse moving when the heart doesn't move. Therefore, intermittent pulse is nothing more than intermittent heart activity. It is truly because the heart's movement is interrupted. Why does the heart move? Because it is stimulated. How can the heart contract when stimulated? Because muscles, when stimulated, can contract, and the heart is composed of muscles, so it also contracts when stimulated. Why does the heart's movement stop? Because the stimulation is abnormal, or the pathways transmitting the stimulation are obstructed. The heart is just a small object, so stimulating it should affect the entire heart. Why must there be transmission pathways? Because the heart is divided into upper and lower sections; the upper part consists of the left and right atria, and the lower part consists of the left and right ventricles. Both the atria and ventricles are muscular, but they are separated by connective tissue, each independent and not connected. Therefore, there must be transmission devices so that stimulation in one area can be transmitted to another. Now we know that the heart's stimulation originates from the sinus venosus, located in the upper half of the right atrium, near the entry point of venous blood into the right atrium. Stimulation here is transmitted to the ventricles via transmission pathways, so atrial contraction is followed by ventricular contraction. Ventricular contraction is necessary for blood to be expelled, so the pulse's movement entirely depends on ventricular contraction, and the heart's contraction entirely depends on stimulation. Additionally, there is a special state that must be understood. During the heart's contraction and early expansion phases, if external stimulation is applied to the heart again, the heart will not respond at this time, so it will not contract again. This is called the "refractory period," and this phenomenon has a great relationship with the explanation of intermittent pulse.

The heart's original stimulation, originating near the sinus venosus, has a fixed and unchanging duration, so the heart's contraction and relaxation are orderly. Now, if a special stimulation occurs in the ventricles, not periodically and not within the refractory period, the heart will be stimulated and contract again, and the pulse will arrive again. This contraction is shorter in time than the previous normal contraction, so the pulse arrives twice in succession. After the premature contraction, the normal stimulation arrives again, but if it falls within the refractory period, the heart will not be affected, so it cannot cause contraction. Contraction must wait for the next normal stimulation, so the resting time is longer, and the pulse stops. In general, the pulse is like "arriving twice in succession with a slight pause." The old saying that the intermittent pulse can return on its own is "a slight pause followed by two successive arrivals," which is incorrect. If one normal contraction and one premature contraction arrive alternately, it will seem like "a slight pause followed by two successive arrivals," but in essence, it is still just "arriving twice in succession with a slight pause." The old saying reversed the order. In light of this, the old saying that the pulse that stops but can return on its own is an intermittent pulse is actually the ventricular premature contraction of today. However, when premature contraction arrives, if the amount of blood contained in the ventricles is still very small, then even if the heart contracts, the amount of blood expelled is insufficient to cause a clear expansion of the artery, becoming the pulseless contraction described above, and the subsequent normal contraction is obscured by the refractory period. One must wait for the next normal contraction to see the pulse, so the time without a pulse is even longer. Because there is no phenomenon of two successive arrivals, it feels like one pulse is missing when palpated. The old saying calls this unable to return on its own, calling it an alternating pulse. In fact, although the pulse is like this, listening to the heart clearly reveals the sound of premature contraction, which can prove it. The old method of distinguishing between intermittent and alternating pulses based on whether the pulse that stops can return on its own to predict good or bad outcomes. Little did they know that merely feeling the pulse without listening to the heart, even if the heart can return on its own, the pulse may be like it cannot return! This is something the old doctors discussing the pulse could not have dreamed of.

Atrioventricular Conduction Block occurs when the pathway from the atria to the ventricles is obstructed. In mild cases, the function of transmission from the atria to the ventricles is not very sensitive, and the transmission time is prolonged. Therefore, the distance of each heart contraction gradually increases, until a certain point when the ventricles do not respond to the stimulation from the atria. At this time, the pulse stops and misses one beat. After a short pause, the transmission function returns to its original state, so the distance of contraction temporarily shortens somewhat, and then gradually lengthens again, until it no longer responds and stops. Therefore, the pulse of this condition is inevitably slow, which aligns with the "palpate it and it comes slowly" mentioned by Zhang Zhongjing. After the pause, the subsequent pulse comes faster than before. This is also what is called returning on its own, which also aligns with Zhang Zhongjing's description of intermittent yin pulse. Therefore, atrioventricular conduction block is also Zhang Zhongjing's intermittent pulse. (For details, refer to "Critique of Huang Han Medicine".) (End of Typhoid Fever, Part Five)

Common Knowledge Q&A About Diseases 184

— Cheng Hanzhang

(67) Laryngeal Tuberculosis and Laryngeal Syphilis

(Q) What is laryngeal tuberculosis?

(A) It is tuberculosis of the larynx secondary to pulmonary tuberculosis (consumption); primary laryngeal tuberculosis is rare.

(Q) What are the initial symptoms of laryngeal tuberculosis?

(A) The patient has a stubborn, incurable hoarseness, cough, and phlegm.

(Q) What happens later?

(A) Complains of sore throat, with pain worsening when swallowing; ulcers appear in the larynx. If the ulcer is in the arytenoid cartilage region, the pain radiates to the ear; if the ulcer is in the anterior wall of the pharynx and epiglottis region, then the pain occurs when swallowing.

(Q) Do patients with laryngeal tuberculosis have any unusual speech?

(A) The voice changes; after the ulcer appears, there is "loss of voice."

(Q) Can other symptoms be combined with laryngeal tuberculosis at the same time?

(A) Often complicated by glottic edema and chondritis of the larynx.

(Q) When diagnosing, what types of throat diseases should it be distinguished from?

(A) It should be distinguished from laryngeal syphilis and laryngeal cancer.

(Q) What is the prognosis for patients with laryngeal tuberculosis?

(A) Most are incurable.

(Q) How is it treated?

(A) First, patients should be prohibited from talking and smoking; pay attention to overall nutrition.

(Q) What medications are used locally in the larynx?

(A) Apply peppermint oil (20%) or lactic acid solution (25-30%) to the throat. Cocaine solution can be used for pain relief.

(Q) Are there any internal medications?

(A) Take calcium agents or creosote internally. Inject calcium gluconate.

(Q) What should be done if the patient has difficulty breathing due to swelling of the throat?

(A) A tracheostomy must be performed.

(Q) What is laryngeal syphilis?

(A) That is, during the second stage of syphilis, condyloma lata appear in the larynx, resulting in conjunctivitis, congestion, and redness, even glottic edema. Or in the third stage, gummas form in the arytenoid cartilage and vocal cord region, destroying tissue and forming ulcers in the larynx. This is called laryngeal syphilis.

(Q) What are the symptoms of laryngeal syphilis?

(A) Like laryngeal tuberculosis, it causes hoarseness and difficulty swallowing.

(Q) Are there any complications when suffering from laryngeal syphilis?

(A) Often complicated by perichondritis of the larynx and glottic edema.

(Q) When diagnosing laryngeal syphilis, what diseases should it be distinguished from?

(A) It should be distinguished from laryngeal tuberculosis and cancer.

(Q) What is the treatment for laryngeal tuberculosis?

(A) Nothing more than the administration of anti-syphilitic therapy, which includes injections of 606, 914, mercury, and bismuth, internal administration of iodine, etc.

High Blood Pressure and Arteriosclerosis (Part 2) 185

— Yueqi

—Medical Story No. 9—

Another hypothesis is based on such a commonly known fact that people with high blood pressure have very clear changes in the kidneys. So some people imagine that because, in such a situation, the kidneys do not eliminate all wastes in the body, so some kind of waste remaining in the blood causes blood vessels to contract and move throughout the body. However, it is very difficult to find any waste in the body that has this kind of property. The famous Doctor Batty-Shaw of Tuton resolutely stated some years ago that there are no intermediate products of nutrients that can cause blood vessels to contract. But Major discovered not long ago that Guanidine, which is formed by the disintegration of protein food, contains this kind of material.

Major also discovered that injecting liver extracts can lower blood pressure, and its effect lasts for a long time. The theory on which this discovery is based is like this: We know that the liver is related to the production of uric acid. Uric acid is probably made from some intermediate products such as "guanidine" by the liver. For some reason, the liver cannot make uric acid from these products, so they continue to circulate in the blood. We know that they will increase blood pressure. Liver extracts in the blood will synthesize them into non-toxic uric acid, so the materials that increase blood pressure are eliminated from the blood, and the blood will also fall.

However, doctors with diagnostic experience will rise up to argue against this hypothesis: If "guanidine" is the cause of high blood pressure, then why does "guanidine" only begin to work at the age of fifty or sixty? Also, if this is caused by bad teeth, then some people have bad teeth at a young age, but high blood pressure must wait until they are fifty or sixty years old before it starts.

Generally speaking, high blood pressure is a hereditary disease. In the eyes of ordinary people, doctors do not need to spend much thought on this kind of observation. In fact, on the contrary, for various reasons, this is one of the most difficult topics to reach. Think about it: any doctor only lives one lifetime; therefore, it is difficult for him to observe the diseases of parents and children at the same age. Of course, the patient will tell him the parents’ symptoms and the cause of death: but the doctor is quite difficult to believe such narratives! Partly because he does not believe the patient’s description of his own symptoms, and partly because the patient often frankly expresses suspicion about the parents’ diseases. Moreover, modern doctors do not completely agree with the conclusions that biology has reached regarding heredity.

Only one hypothesis is consistent with all situations, because it is in line with the latest conclusions regarding "creation." This hypothesis is that protoplasm has a tendency, that is, at a certain stage of an individual's life, certain body cells! Such as the aorta, the membranes of blood, etc., and the microvessels of the kidneys, etc.! Certain changes will occur. Under this hypothesis, we can infer that high blood pressure and arteriosclerosis are only a physiological law of aging in the human body.

In terms of treatment, the only valuable treatment is to adjust the general lifespan by reducing the pressure applied to the blood vessels. In this way, lifespan can indeed be extended for several years. But the so-called reducing the pressure on blood vessels does not mean that all activities in the world should stop. It is a huge mistake to measure the improvement of human life by recording falling blood pressure, or to imagine that this is possible. Some doctors have measured the blood pressure of the parties involved in life insurance companies over the years. This is a dull and monotonous occupation. But they also gained several benefits from this. One is that they learn what situations can be affected by treatment and what situations are not affected. In general, high blood pressure and arteriosclerosis are difficult to treat. In New York, in Chicago, in Vienna, in Berlin, in Paris, and in London, various methods of treating high blood pressure and arteriosclerosis have been tried, but none have been effective.

In short, changes in blood pressure have nothing to do with health. People with higher blood pressure are not necessarily weaker than those with lower blood pressure. High blood pressure is not a disease, but just a physiological adjustment. Clindening published an interesting piece of advice in "The Human Body" saying:

"It is best not to let people over the age of fifty know their blood pressure records, because this will cause unpleasant news. Don't give up your work, your entertainment, or, for women, don't give up your political campaigns. Life is for living, for complete happiness and activity. You must not look at the mercury shaking in the glass tube with fearful eyes and let the flame of life go out unnaturally."

Domestically Produced Medicinal Plants 186

— Zhou Mengbai, Lin Hongzao

Embryophyta, Siphcnogama Section of Higher Plants; Angiospermae Subsection of Flowering Plants; Dicoyledoneae Class of Dicotyledons; Melachlamydeae Subclass of Choripetalae; Compositae Family of Composites; (1) Burdock, *Arctium Lappa* L., Klette (German), Burdock (English)

Plant

Originally from Europe, cultivated in drylands, a biennial herb. Roots are fleshy, growing straight down. Stems are about 1-1.5 meters tall. Leaves have long petioles, broad and heart-shaped, with dentate edges. The underside of the leaves is densely covered with cottony hairs. Terminal corymbose inflorescences bear purple flowers in summer, consisting solely of tubular florets forming a head.

Crude Drug

Burdock Fruit (Aggressive Seed) *Fructus Bardanae* is harvested from the fruit of the burdock plant, and is oblong, slightly curved, about 5 mm long, and no more than 2 mm wide. The exterior has prominent grey ridges, with an oily odor and a slightly bitter taste.

Components

The roots contain inulin (45%) and fats, with the general composition as follows (% in dried product): crude protein 12.3, ash 3.6, carbohydrates 69.0, crude fat 0.82. Fresh roots contain approximately 73% water. The fruit contains 25-30% fat, and the leaves contain mucilage, tannins, and essential oils (0.03%).

Medicinal Use

Traditionally, burdock is said to have diuretic effects and is used for edema or sore throats, fresh sores, and poisons from venomous insects and snakes. The daily dose is 8 grams, prepared as a decoction. An example prescription is Burdock Fruit Decoction, which is effective for various throat pains: Burdock Fruit 8.0, Scrophularia, Rhinoceros Horn, Cimicifuga, Scutellaria, Akebia, Platycodon, and Licorice, each 4.0. The above is a decoction of 200.0, taken three times a day after meals. In European folk medicine, burdock root (*Radix Bardanae*, English/American/German) has long been used as a diuretic or for syphilis and mercury poisoning.

Popular Lectures on Modern Venereology (10) (7) 187

— Chen Shengbai (Compiled), Yin Muqiang (Proofread)

Part Four: Lymphogranuloma Venereum

2. Swelling of the Inguinal Lymph Nodes: This is a characteristic symptom. Approximately three to four weeks after infection, swelling of the inguinal lymph nodes can be palpated, also known colloquially as "groin buboes." The onset of this swelling is slow, and its course is protracted, one of its distinguishing features. The swelling begins as being the size of a broad bean or a fingertip, and then gradually grows to the size of a goose egg or a fist. Each lymph node develops separately, without coalescing, a second distinguishing feature. When the swollen lymph nodes adhere to the skin, the skin appears flushed. As the disease progresses further, the centers of the glands soften, gradually ulcerating and discharging pus, forming multiple non-fusing fistulous tracts. This is a third distinguishing feature. Around the softened lesions, the proliferation of granulation tissue is often palpable as a raised, hard glandular tissue, a fourth distinguishing feature. Recurrent bouts of fever are a fifth distinguishing feature. As for other systemic symptoms, they are milder than those associated with chancroidal buboes, but their course is more prolonged.

3. Symptoms Beyond the Inguinal Lymph Nodes: Among these, lesions of the external genitalia and perineum, especially in the anus and rectum of women, are primary, due to the different distribution of lymph nodes compared to men. I will now describe this in detail:

A. Elephantiasis of the External Genitalia: In women, the labia majora and minora swell and subside irregularly, ultimately leading to elephantiasis-like thickening. In men, the prepuce and penis swell and harden, resulting in phimosis or abnormal enlargement of the penis. All of these are due to lymphatic fluid stagnation caused by inflammation of the accessory glands.

B. Perineal, Anal, and Rectal Symptoms: Lymph from the female genitals does not flow into the inguinal glands but rather into the pelvic cavity and the rectal wall. Therefore, in clinical practice, swelling of the lymph nodes in the deep labia of the perineum, the anal region, and the rectal wall is commonly seen, or they may form hard infiltrations, and also suppurate, becoming fistulous tracts. Conversely, lesions of the inguinal lymph nodes are less common. Furthermore, lesions of the rectal wall often cause rectal stricture due to scar contraction after fistula healing, leading to constipation or stools as thin as sheep intestines. Alternatively, persistent unhealed fistulae may discharge mucous and bloody stools, leading to suspicion of hemorrhoidal fistulae or hemorrhoids.

B. Diagnosis: The characteristic state of glandular swelling is the diagnostic marker, such as hard cords, localized central suppuration of the glands, slow progression, all of which are key diagnostic points. However, there may also be a lack of characteristic signs, such as elephantiasis of the external genitalia, or atypical symptoms involving the anorectal region. Therefore, accurate diagnosis relies on the so-called Frei test.

The Frei test, discovered by Frei in 1925, is essential for differentiating this condition. Its procedure is similar to the Benshade method. Knowledge of this test belongs to specialists, so it will not be described here in detail.

The following should be discussed in the differential diagnosis:

A. Syphilitic Bubo: Can be distinguished by its non-suppurating nature, the presence of an initial chancre in the genital area, a positive test for *Treponema pallidum*, and a positive Wassermann test.

B. Gonorrheal Bubo: Can be distinguished by its acute course, severe subjective symptoms, and the co-occurrence of gonorrhea.

C. Chancroidal Bubo: Can be distinguished by its acute course, marked redness, pain, fever, and the presence of a chancroid in the genital area.

D. Hemorrhoidal Fistulae and Hemorrhoids: Should be differentiated in atypical cases beyond the inguinal lymph nodes. This can be done by considering the more severe local changes in lymphogranuloma venereum, the induration or ulceration around the fistulous tracts, a positive Frei skin reaction, and an inquiry into the patient's history.

C. Treatment and Prevention: Treatment of this disease includes bed rest, local dressings, incision, radiation, the administration of astringents and alteratives, and specific antigen injection therapy. In addition, the intravenous injection of sulfonamide drugs has proven quite effective. Prevention can be based on general methods for preventing venereal diseases. (End of full text)

A Brief Discussion of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (6) (5) 188

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 12: Treatment of Pulmonary Tuberculosis

Can Pulmonary Tuberculosis Be Cured?

Whenever pulmonary tuberculosis treatment is mentioned, I think everyone must ask: Can pulmonary tuberculosis really be cured? This question is undoubtedly complex and difficult to answer easily, but various facts point undeniably towards an affirmative answer. We must understand that among ordinary pulmonary tuberculosis patients, even those with tubercle bacilli detected in their sputum, cases of complete recovery without recurrence are frequently seen in clinical practice. Furthermore, there is much clear evidence in pathological anatomy. In corpses that died from other diseases, old tuberculous lesions are often found at the apex of the lungs; inside the caseous bronchial glands there are also calcareous remnants. All of this sufficiently proves that the recovery of pulmonary tuberculosis is beyond doubt. In this well-managed tuberculosis, the fibrous connective tissue around the lesion is particularly abundant. As for the caseous matter, it is sealed off to prevent the spread of tubercle bacilli. The more the fibrous connective tissue is produced, the more firmly the caseous matter is sealed off. As a result, small lesions are mostly completely curable. However, these sealed and surrounded lesions can easily cause a recurrence of the disease if the opportunity arises. Although this recurrence does not necessarily account for the majority, the possibility exists for every patient. The time is also uncertain; even old lesions of more than ten years are treated the same way. Moreover, even if the lesion here is in a state of recovery, it can occur elsewhere. Therefore, whether pulmonary tuberculosis can be cured is not a question. But to what extent can we say that it will not recur? No one can answer this question.

The Medical Treatment of Pain (31) 189

— Li Yu

Headache

Headache is a very common ailment. Some people suffer from frequent headaches, while others experience them occasionally. Because it is such a common problem, countless individuals make a living by manufacturing and selling headache remedies. Before the age of scientific medicine, when people had headaches, they simply took whatever medicine someone told them was effective, without asking why they had the headache or how the remedy worked. Not only patients acted this way, but also those who called themselves physicians. The fundamental mistakes were: First, not knowing why the headache occurred; second, not knowing how the pain reliever worked. Now is the age of scientific progress. For any disease, we must first understand the cause. We must also know the chemical composition of the medicine we take, how it works inside the body, how it enters the body, and how it is excreted. This way, we can both prevent headaches and treat them with appropriate or fundamental methods. I will briefly describe the causes of headaches and the principles of treatment:

Generally speaking, there is a reason for every headache. If there is no reason, the head will not hurt. There are many causes of headaches, so different headaches cannot be treated in the same way. Conversely, the same treatment cannot cure all headaches. If it could, it would only be a superficial method or a form of anesthesia, not a fundamental solution.

Free Talk

A Watershed in Creative Methods 190

— Zhiying

Luigi Pirandello recently told reporters in New York that his creations originated in his mind. This statement actually contains a very important question: Does art originate solely from the "mind" in isolation, or is it merely processed by the mind?

Artistic creation undoubtedly requires imagination, even "fantasy." If there were no activity in the writer's "mind," would art even exist in the world? However, the crux of the matter lies precisely here. Does our mind automatically create things out of thin air, or is it merely an advanced material structure that produces imaginations reflecting or related to these real things due to the influence and stimulation of real things?

Modern philosophy has provided us with a clear answer to this question. The human mind, human thought, is stimulated by its real environment, reflecting and expressing it.

So, are Pirandello's words wrong? Is Pirandello's art a reflection of reality?

In fact, Pirandello's words, as an indication of his artistic creation method, are not entirely wrong. And his art is not a reflection of reality; this does not contradict our explanation above.

Originally, there are two main different tendencies in artistic creation methods: one is realistic, and the other is idealistic. This is like a "watershed" in the torrent of philosophical history, dividing into materialism and idealism. However, in reality, realism and materialism, idealism and idealism, although they maintain close relationships, are not entirely the same.

Idealistic writers advocate replacing the objective with the subjective. They believe that all subjectivity accurately reflects reality. Therefore, writers must be as bold as possible in expressing their subjectivity in order to be faithful to reality. Everything expressed by subjectivity is "real." Subjectivity creates everything.

Oscar Wilde said in "The Decay of Lying": "Art never expresses anything but itself. It has an independent life, just as Thought has, and develops purely on its own lines. It is not mimetic, but creative. Nature is often largely disappointing. In fact, Nature is usually disappointing. It is only in Art that we can see the natural course of things. It is in Art that we get what we desire. Morever, Nature is our creation. It is in our brain that it quickens to life. Things are because we see them, and what we see, and how we see it, depends on the Arts that have influenced us. To look at a thing is very different from seeing a thing. One does not see anything until one sees its beauty."

These words are all "substantial," so I have copied a large section. It seems that we do not need to spend more space here on these opinions. We simply have one question here: According to this, what does the artist "depend on" to exist? If Wilde himself can completely prove that he was not born from a mother's womb but "depended" on something to survive, then we might believe his words.

Here we see a tendency of idealism: to make everything in reality "depend on" one's own subjectivity, "depend on" one's own art. In this sense, Pirandello's statement that his creation originated in his mind is not incorrect. Because Pirandello is also such an idealistic writer, and we say that their art does not reflect reality is not wrong either, because they are not expressing reality but "subjectivity." Their art cannot create vivid images of reality but is only a "conceptual game," a "verbal magic."

The so-called "subjectivity" is created by the real living environment. But if we therefore say that being faithful to "subjectivity" is faithfully expressing the complex living environment, this is undoubtedly an overly arbitrary oversight. It is precisely because subjectivity is created by the conditions of social life that, under the conditions of contradictory and divided social life, there is a "subjectivity" that represents the realistic elements of uniting these contradictory and divided social relations, enabling them to reach a higher development; and there is also a "subjectivity" that represents some decadent elements of reality, which is the opposite. The former "subjectivity" does not sing loudly of absolute independence; it often clings to the developing elements of reality because its creative method is realism. The latter "subjectivity," although also an expression of the decadent elements of reality, does not dare to truthfully express its decadent reality, let alone express the developing reality; otherwise, it would have ceased to exist long ago. This kind of "subjectivity," as a phenomenon of decadent real elements, hides in its own narrow "subjectivity," creating things that distort reality.

These two different subjectivities are the watershed in artistic creation methods. They both come from reality, but one will express reality, and the other will distort reality. People like Wilde and Pirandello, who constantly uphold subjectivity, end up killing subjectivity instead because they treat subjectivity as a symbol to defend sins, as a kind of empty waste, and not as a practical, active force, a force that coincides with the development of reality and supports reality.

Autumn Waters Share the Same Color as the Long Sky 191

Dusk in Huaibin 192

— Shen Shengshi

When teaching in Huaiyuan, I felt a bit tired after finishing a day of classes. It was impossible to find a place to dispel the gloom in the city. After dinner, I often went to the banks of the Huai River with Er and Hong.

It was dusk, after the setting sun.

The light footsteps of the three of us, rustling, went along the stone-chipped road paved with green shade. While talking and walking, the cool evening breeze flowed from the wheat fields on both sides to the body, taking away the tiredness of the day. Hong often hummed a song; or made a weird cry "Ooh—", listening to the echoes from the surrounding mountains colliding back, also echoing "Ooh—".

A rushing, long stream lay horizontally in front of us. The faint moonlight reflected the silvery waves on the water. I loved listening to the "surging gurgling" sound of the water, a great and peaceful natural music, which struck the vast love in my soul, giving me a vast and open state of mind.

Together with Ji and Hong, we sat down on the stone steps of the wharf built by the foreign pastor on the bank.

At our feet, the rushing water hit the waves, rushing down to the lower reaches. Looking at the towering mountains on both sides from afar, the mountains stood upright with a solemn appearance. The moon, embracing the clouds, sprinkled a silvery light from the top of the mountain.

In this realm, I breathed out refreshingly, recalling two lines of poetry from the corner of my heart.

——Mountains follow the flat wilderness, the river enters the vast wasteland.

Draped in silvery moonlight, taking advantage of the cool breeze rising on the river, we walked down the stone steps, along the shallows of the Huai River. The rushing water rolled and ran at my feet, and the rising waves splashed onto the back of my feet. Dimly on the water, a few red lights shone from afar, a night shift transport ship dragging seven or eight large boats broke through the waves and rushed over. As the boat passed, the water waves struck up thousands of golden snakes; listen to the long whistle echoing from the mountain wall.

I love the dusk in Huaibin, unfolding a magnificent night view.

On "Tangerines" 193

— Chen Zizhan

"Traveling across sand and water to the mountain corner,

Thorned branches encircling the house.

Abundant with patterned, round fruits ripening,

In this, the finest flavor comes from heaven."

This is a small poem I wrote ten years ago, published in a small literary magazine called "Odds and Ends" edited by Luo Hezhi and published in Changsha. At that time, I was teaching at the first Normal School of Hunan Province and the Normal School of Changsha County. Hei Zhi asked me where I moved to, so I wrote this little poem to him. Hei Zhi smiled and said to me: "Your poem is not good, but the place where you live is good." I also smiled and said to him: "The reason I moved to the foot of Yuelu Mountain, traveling across continents and waters, is precisely because there are tangerine trees, evergreen all year round, surrounding the house. I can eat the red tangerines of Yuelu from late autumn to early spring!"

Leaving Changsha from the South Gate, crossing the river, and passing through Shuiluzhou, you arrive at the foot of Yuelu Mountain. The area near the river and against the mountain is all tangerine orchards. Shuiluzhou was called Tangerine Isle in ancient times, precisely because it was named for growing tangerines. Du Fu's poem "Two Temples on Yuelu Mountain, Daolin" has a line that says, "The fields and land on Qiaozhou are still fertile," because the fields and land on the isle are fertile, the tangerines produced are large and sweet. According to local gazettes, "Tanzhou Tangerine Isle is south of the county, facing Nan Jin. It often looks as if it is below. When the summer waters embrace the mountains, all the isles and sandbars are submerged, the isle alone remains." Ancient people thought that Tangerine Isle could rise and fall with the water level, which is inevitably close to mythology.

We know that tangerine trees are a specialty of Hunan, famous since ancient times. Qu Yuan's "Ode to the Tangerine" says: "Heaven and Earth, auspicious trees, tangerines come to serve. Receiving fate, not migrating, born in the south." It seems to say that Heaven and Earth specially ordered tangerine trees to be born in this southern country. Of course, the southern country mentioned by Qu Yuan does not necessarily refer to Hunan, but it is a fact that Hunan was a part of the State of Chu at that time and happened to be in the south of the State of Chu. The "Ode to the Tangerine" also says: "Deep and difficult to move, protect even more. The green leaves are luxuriant, delightful. Overlapping branches are thorny, round and clustered. Green and yellow mixed, patterns dazzling. Pure color inside is white, suitable for the Way. Flourishing and ornate, beautiful and not ugly." Qu Yuan personified the tangerine tree, saying that it has three virtues: one is firm ambition, the second is dazzling patterns, and the third is an essence not ugly. In fact, Qu Yuan himself wanted to use the tangerine tree to symbolize his own personality, so his "Ode to the Tangerine" is nothing more than self-praise.

Tangerine trees belong to the Rutaceae family in botany, evergreen shrubs, the trunk is about ten feet high, the branches are very dense and thorny, the leaves are long oval, the leaf tips are sharp, and the petioles have winged small pieces. In summer, five-petaled white flowers bloom, slightly similar to jasmine, with a fragrant aroma. After frost falls, the oblate fruits ripen, the peel turns red, and then they can be eaten. Wang Youjun's letter said: "Offering three hundred tangerines, before the frost falls, not many can be obtained." Originally, if the tangerines do not see the frost, and the peel does not turn red, then they are not good to eat. Wei Yingwu has a line in his poem that says: "After writing, I want to inscribe three hundred fruits, Dongting must wait for the frost to fill the forest." He is using the allusion from Wang Youjun's letter. (To be continued)

Middle Age 194

— Lingmo

Lately, I've been constantly touched by the feelings of autumn, which, in turn, has brought on the oppressive feeling of middle age. Those who habitually compare the four seasons to the stages of human life say that middle age is close to summer. However, it seems difficult for us to see a middle age that resembles summer. Most people, upon reaching middle age, already have the air of old age, and their lives continue in the same pattern forever after. To put it nicely, this is probably because reason has grown significantly and knowledge has become established. To put it badly, even if we set aside the unfortunate issues of declining vitality and career anxieties, and even if we acknowledge that they can indeed find a proper way to live and establish themselves in middle age, it's not much different from the life of a superstitious person.

We often hear people talk about the sentiments of middle age, but these so-called sentiments are probably just feelings of helplessness, or recollections of past sentiments. The genuine sadness of youth is no longer there. From various theories, we know that the elimination of sadness is both inevitable and necessary, but the inevitable process and necessary conditions here may not have a consistent explanation. People's desire for spring to warm up sooner and autumn to cool down sooner often contradicts the actual seasonal changes. Who knows if our sentimentality disappears too quickly?

Does everyone go through a period of sentimental age? It seems impossible to know. And if the era is one in which one should not be sentimental, then personal sentimentality is insignificant. But if this era is full of sentimental people who forcibly endure the oppression of the era and try to conceal their sentimentality, wouldn't it form a great hypocrisy? Although unnatural progress may not be a form of progress and may not gradually turn into nature, one must also worry about the breaking of an empty shell.

I don't want to think about it anymore. Let's narrow it down to the individual. The states of "establishment" and "unconfusion" certainly seem like perfection. However, since there is a way to complete it in a model-like way, the value of the achievement is extremely uneven. The weaknesses inherent in middle age may not be immediately apparent, but once one approaches old age, one either falls into stubbornness or succumbs to decline. These two characteristics, which are regarded as features of aging, are actually deeply buried in middle age. This situation is too common, making us think that it should naturally be so, and never think that it can be noticed earlier in middle age. Although the so-called sentiments of middle age are often the approaching of summer's decline and old age, at the same time, one often believes that one is in a very confident middle age. As long as one firmly grasps oneself in middle age, old age will not come immediately. Isn't this precisely stubbornness and confusion?

People's feelings about their own middle age are not as clear as their feelings about autumn. After all, autumn belongs to the outside world. Of course, there should be many differences between the outside world and the inner world, but if we think that life is a longer period, it is not okay to extend it further. We might as well believe that the seasons are a more eternal phenomenon. If we can understand the complexity of autumn, perhaps our middle age will not be so monotonous.

But alas, it is already the autumn of middle age. I don't feel the desolation of autumn in my mood, nor do I appreciate the seriousness of autumn. I really fear that an earlier old age has already arrived.

Night in the Capital of Sakurajima 195

— Green Leaves

Outside the door, the flower market is like a painting; a scene of revelry by licentious foreign gentlemen and socialites, teasing my melancholy mood. I sit in the coffee shop in agony. In the exchange of wine, fragrance, meat, and lust, there is the dance of noble mummies. Filled with inexplicable sorrow, I gaze at the rapid chaos of the city.

Seesaw (6) 196

— Baichen

The little monk also beat the drum: "That board is fun!"

Unexpectedly, Mom gave them a "Ptooey!" and dragged them away: "That will break your legs!"

The little rascal broke free, twisting his body and humming: "......!" The little monk ran back to the door to watch, grabbing the railing and refusing to let go. Inside, the board seesawed up and down, climbed up and slid down on the high frame, and people became one, laughing as one. No one paid attention to them.

"The one at Guihua Nunnery is more fun! Let's go! That one has --"

Mom forcefully pulled the little monk away, coaxing them with something or other. The children softened their hearts, looked back a few times, and had no choice but to leave.

Behind them, there was a burst of shouting, a burst of laughter, and the little monk only felt his body relax, a sudden sinking feeling, and a "thump" sound behind him, and the little monk's legs couldn't help but stiffen.

Turn left, turn right, the sound was no longer heard, the white powder wall was also gone, and the children followed behind Mom.

There were more people on the road, and the women carried incense, small lanterns, and yellow cloth bags, talking and walking in groups of three and five. Turn another bend, and you see a screen wall painted with yellow powder. Opposite the screen wall is a temple. People are squeezed in front of the temple like ants. The noisy sounds mixed into a sea, and you can't make heads or tails of it. Only the small candy gong clangs, and the bamboo clapper bangs alone, above this sea of sounds. They could hear that the "duo er duo" bamboo clapper was Dad's. Inside the temple gate, it was pitch black, and only a burst of thick green smoke could be seen billowing outwards, slowly dissipating on the roof.

Gradually walking into the crowd, Mom found Dad's carrying pole. Dad was busy. While ladling porridge, while collecting money, while washing bowls, he also took time to knock the bamboo clapper twice. The carrying pole was surrounded by people, and Dad seemed unable to take care of it. Mom wanted to help, but Dad pushed her away: "Go burn your incense!"

The three squeezed into the temple gate, and a burst of smoke rushed towards them, blurring their eyes with tears. In the courtyard, there was a large money pot, burning dozens or hundreds of small lanterns, and the flames were still two feet high. It was so hot that people were sweating. In a small pot, whole strands of incense were burning, and candles were also thrown in to burn. The smoke was like rainbows, and you couldn't see people across the way: the smell of candle wax was suffocating. The women chanted: "Amitabha," and the sound of copper coins thrown into the money cage rang out with a clang.

Mom kowtowed, telling ghost stories. She pressed the children to kowtow as well. The little monk ran back to the courtyard first. He called out: "Let's go! It's not fun." Mom had no choice but to lead the little rascal out as well. But she was confused and didn't even take a look at the Bodhisattva! Turning back, she was blinded by the smoke again, so she had to pray two more ghost words before walking out of the temple gate.
